=== b'How to reset a lost or forgotten password' ===

b'How to reset a lost or forgotten Twitter password\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nTo reset your password, you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll need access to the phone number or email associated with your Twitter account. This verification information helps ensure your account is only accessible to you. If you can\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t access your phone or email, you won\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t be able to recover your password, and may need to sign up for a new account.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nWhat you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll need to change your password on Twitter\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nAn accurate and up-to-date email address, and/or phone number\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0ensure you never lose access to your Twitter account. There are a few ways to change your password, and keeping this information up to date simplifies resetting your account or password.'


=== b'How to reset a lost or forgotten password' ===

b"How to change your password while you're logged in\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      For IOS:\n    \n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nFrom the navigation menu\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0, tap Settings and privacy.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nTap Your account.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nTap\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Change your password.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nEnter your current password.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 5\n          \n\nEnter your New password.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 6\n          \n\nEnter your new password again to\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Confirm password.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 7\n          \n\nTap Done to save your changes.\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nNote: If you can log in but can't remember your password, you can send yourself a password reset email from the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0password settings page.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Additionally, you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll be logged out of all your active Twitter sessions, except for the one you use to change your password.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      For Android:\n    \n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nFrom the navigation menu\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0, tap Settings and privacy.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nTap Your account.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nTap\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Change your password.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nEnter your current password.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 5\n          \n\nEnter your New password.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 6\n          \n\nEnter your new password again to\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Confirm password.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 7\n          \n\nTap Done to save your changes.\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nNote: If you can log in but can't remember your password, you can send yourself a password reset email from the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0password settings page.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Additionally, you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll be logged out of all your active Twitter sessions, except for the one you use to change your password.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      For Desktop:\n    \n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nFrom your desktop, click on the More\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon in the navigation bar and select\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Settings and privacy.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nFrom\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Your account, click on\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Change your password.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nEnter your Current password.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nEnter your New password.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 5\n          \n\nEnter your new password again to Confirm password.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 6\n          \n\nClick Save.\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nNote: If you're able to log in but can't remember your password, you can send yourself a password reset email from the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0password settings page.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Additionally, you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll be logged out of all your active Twitter sessions, except for the one you use to change your password.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to reset your Twitter password via email\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nFrom the sign in page on either twitter.com, mobile.twitter.com, or the Twitter for iOS or Android app, click\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Forgot password?Enter your email address, phone number, or Twitter username. If you have multiple accounts associated with your phone number, you cannot use your phone number during this step.Choose the email address where you want to receive the password reset email.Check your email inbox. Twitter will immediately send a message to your account's email address.The email will include a code which will be valid for 60 minutes.Enter this code into the text field on the password reset page and click Submit.When prompted, choose a new password.\n\n\n\n\nNote:\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Resetting your password will log you out of all your active Twitter sessions.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to reset your Twitter password via text\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nIf you've added your phone number to your account in your\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0settings, you may receive a password reset via text message.\n\nFrom the Forgot password? page, enter your phone number, email address, or Twitter username.\nEnter your phone number and click Search.Text a code to my phone ending in [XX] will be displayed. Click Continue.Twitter will text you a code which will be valid for 60 minutes.Enter this code into the text field on the password reset page and click Submit.You will then be prompted to choose a new password.\n\n\n\n\nNote:\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Resetting your password will log you out of all your active Twitter sessions. Additionally, password reset via text message isn't available to accounts that are enrolled in login verification. You can only reset your password through email."

=== b'How to reset a lost or forgotten password' ===

b'Twitter password reset FAQs\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nI tried resetting my Twitter account or password, but I still can\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t log into my account. What should I do?\n\nIf you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re still having\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0login issues\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0after resetting your Twitter password, you may be\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0locked out\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0of your account for security purposes.\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nWhat if I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99m not receiving texts or verification codes from Twitter?\n\nYou\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll want to make sure you have cell reception or internet access, and that the Twitter number isn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t blocked. It can take a few minutes to receive a verification code. If you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re still having trouble, try the email password reset option.\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nHow do I reset my Twitter password without email or a phone number?\n\nWe use your email address and phone number to verify your identity, so when you can\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t access this information, recovery options are limited. If you know your Twitter username, we may be able to help with your login issues.\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nWhy do I keep getting password reset emails?\n\nIf you frequently receive password reset messages that you did not request, it may be a good idea to turn on the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Password reset protection\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0in your account settings and set up\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0two-factor authentication.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          More password help\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nSometimes there are circumstances that lead to losing access to the verification information you need to log into your Twitter account.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0After trying the tips below, if you still can\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t recover your password and access your account, contact\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Twitter Support.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Please note that without an email or phone number to verify your identity, recovery options are limited.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      Recovery tips\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nLog in with the username and password combination you last remember.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Check other platfoms.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Look to see if you are still logged into your account elsewhere like the Twitter app, mobile.twitter.com or TweetDeck.Verify what you can. Try finding your Twitter account with one verifying piece of information like your username to help determine the email or phone associated with your account.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nStart with your username\nEntering a valid username prompts Twitter to ask for the email address associated with your account. Try any possible email address you may have associated with your account. When you provide the valid email, Twitter will ask how you want to reset your password.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nStart with your phone number\n\nIf you can\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t determine the valid email, repeat the process above with possible phone numbers. When you provide the valid phone number, Twitter sends a code to the phone associated with your account so you can reset your password. If you receive a prompt saying more than one Twitter account is associated with a phone number, this option won\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t work for you.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          Share this article\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nTweet'


=== b'How to reset a lost or forgotten password' ===

b'Recovery tips\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nLog in with the username and password combination you last remember.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Check other platfoms.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Look to see if you are still logged into your account elsewhere like the Twitter app, mobile.twitter.com or TweetDeck.Verify what you can. Try finding your Twitter account with one verifying piece of information like your username to help determine the email or phone associated with your account.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nStart with your username\nEntering a valid username prompts Twitter to ask for the email address associated with your account. Try any possible email address you may have associated with your account. When you provide the valid email, Twitter will ask how you want to reset your password.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nStart with your phone number\n\nIf you can\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t determine the valid email, repeat the process above with possible phone numbers. When you provide the valid phone number, Twitter sends a code to the phone associated with your account so you can reset your password. If you receive a prompt saying more than one Twitter account is associated with a phone number, this option won\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t work for you.'


=== b'Timelines' ===

b'About\n\n\nConnecting or removing \n\n\nAvailable tools\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            About\n          \n\n            Connecting or removing \n          \n\n            Available tools\n          \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nThird-party apps are applications built on the Twitter platform by external developers, and are not owned or operated by Twitter. When you connect a third-party app to your Twitter account, you are granting that app access to use your account. Depending on its permissions, an authorized app may be able to obtain information from and use your account in various ways, such as reading your Tweets, seeing who you follow, updating your profile, posting Tweets on your behalf, accessing your Direct Messages, or seeing your email address. You can learn more about the specific access in the App permissions\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0section below. Addiontally you can choose to log out of your active Twitter sessions.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\nNote: You should be cautious before giving any third-party app access to your account. If you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re not comfortable with granting an app access to your account, simply click \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9ccancel\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d on the authorization page to decline the app\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s access. We also suggest you regularly review third-party apps which have access to use your account to confirm that you still want to give them access. You can review and revoke access for apps by visiting the Apps and sessions section of your account settings.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nLogging out of active Twitter sessions\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to log out of your active Twitter sessions\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nSign in to your account.\nFrom your\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Settings and privacy, go to the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Apps and sessions\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0section of your account settings. Below\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Sessions, all of the active login sessions connected to your account will be displayed. You can see the location and time of login.\nIf you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99d like to log out of any of the sessions listed, click the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Log out\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0button next to the session, or click\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Log out all other sessions\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0at the top of the list to end all other sessions at once. Please note that while logging out of a session will prevent further actions from that session such as Tweeting, Liking, and replying, it may not delete data (e.g., Direct Messages) that was previously cached on the device while the session was active.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nApp permissions\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\r\n App permissions\n\r\nThird-party apps may request access to perform different actions using your Twitter account.\nOAuth 1.0a User Context\nApps using OAuth 1.0a User Context may ask for the following permissions to access certain information in your account and take certain actions:\nRead\nApps with read access to your Twitter account will have the ability to:\nProfile information: View your profile information, such as your name, location, description, and profile and header photos. Note that the email address associated with your Twitter account and your phone number are not considered profile information. An app will not be able to view your email address unless you grant the app specific permission to do so.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Tweets: View your Tweets (including details such as the number of times a Tweet has been viewed and the interactions others have with a Tweet) and Tweets from accounts you follow on your timeline, including any protected Tweets.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Account settings: View your account settings, such as your preferred language and time zone.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Other accounts: See who you follow, mute, and block.Lists: View your Lists of Twitter accounts.Collections: View your collections of Tweets.\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nOAuth 1.0a User Context\nApps using OAuth 1.0a User Context may ask for the following permissions:\nRead and Write\nApps with read and write access to your Twitter account will have access to view your information as described in the Read section above, and will also have the ability to:\nProfile information: Update your profile information for you.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nTweets: Post Tweets and media on your behalf, delete Tweets for you, and engage with Tweets posted by others for you (for example, like, un-like, or reply to a Tweet, Retweet, etc.).\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nAccount settings: Manage your account settings for you.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nOther accounts: Follow and unfollow accounts for you, and mute, block, or report accounts on your behalf.\nLists: Create Lists of Twitter accounts for you, manage your Lists (for example, add and remove accounts from Lists) for you, and delete your Lists for you.\nCollections: Create collections of Tweets for you, manage your collections (for example, add and remove Tweets from collections) for you, and delete your collections for you.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\nRead, Write, and Direct Messages\nApps with read, write, and Direct Message access to your Twitter account will have access to view your information and take actions as described above in the Read and Write sections, and will also have the ability to: send Direct Messages for you, view Direct Messages you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve sent and received, and manage and delete your Direct Messages. Remember that each communication participant has their own copy of the communication \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x94 deletion of a Direct Message will remove it from your account, not the accounts of the other participants to the communication.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nEmail Address\nIn addition to the permissions above, apps may also ask for permission to view the email address associated with your Twitter account.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nTwitter Ads\nIf you use Twitter Ads, apps may also ask to:\nAnalytics: Access your advertising data, including your campaigns, audiences, business and ad account information (such as account name, ID, and creation date, business name, timezone, and users), ad account and user settings (such as notification email, contact phone number and extensions, industry type, email subscription settings, and tax settings), and creatives and media.\nCampaign and account management: Access your advertising data as described above, create and manage your advertising data (such as media, creatives, campaigns, and audiences) for you, and manage your account (such as account name, industry type, account and user settings, etc.).\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\nLearn more about granting access to your Twitter Ads account with multi-user login.\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nOAuth 2.0 User Context\nOAuth 2.0 User Context enables a developer to set more granular access for their app. Apps using OAuth 2.0 User Context may may ask for permissions in the following categories:\nRead\nRead permissions define what an app can see in your Twitter account. For example, an app may ask permission to view things like:\nAll the Tweets and Spaces you can view, including Tweets from protected accounts.People who follow you and people you follow.Accounts you\'ve muted and blocked.\nYou\'ll see a list of things an app is requesting permission to view under "Things this App can view."\nWrite\nWrite permissions define what actions an app can take on your behalf. For example, an app may ask permission to do things like:\nTweet and retweet for you.Hide and unhide replies to your Tweets.Follow and unfollow people for you.\nYou\'ll see a list of things an app is requesting permission to do on your behalf under "Things this App can do."\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWe do not share your Twitter password with apps. Remember that when you authorize an app to access your Twitter account or take actions on your behalf, the app may use, store, and share your information in accordance with its own business practices. While app developers agree to abide by our rules and guidelines, we strongly recommend that you review an app\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s terms and privacy policy before you authorize the app to access your account.\nLearn more about our rules and guidelines for third-party app developers in our Developer Policy.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to connect to a third-party app\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nIn the app you want to connect, find the button/link asking you to connect your Twitter account (usually "Connect to Twitter", "Sign in with Twitter" or something similar).\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nDepending on the app, you may be presented with a consent dialog from Twitter asking you to authorize the app to use your account or you may be prompted to grant the app access to the Twitter accounts on your iOS device.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nYou can review the various permissions you are granting to the app. You will see examples of actions the app will be able to perform using your account.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nIf you are routed to a Twitter website and you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re already logged in to your account, use the Authorize app button to connect the app. If you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re not already logged in to your account, you will need to log in. Before you enter your username and password, check that the page is secure by verifying the URL starts with https://twitter.com. If the page is secure, enter your username and password and use the Sign In button to connect the app.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 5\n          \n\nIf you are prompted to grant the app access to the Twitter accounts on your iOS device, use the Connect button to connect the app. If you have multiple Twitter accounts on your device, you may need to select the account that you wish to connect to the app.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nNote: You can always review and revoke access for apps at any time by visiting the Apps and sessions section of your account settings.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nIn the app you want to connect, find the button/link asking you to connect your Twitter account (usually "Connect to Twitter", "Sign in with Twitter" or something similar).\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nDepending on the app, you may be routed to a Twitter website or to the Twitter for Android app to authorize the app to use your account. \n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nYou can review the various permissions you are granting to the app. You will see examples of actions the app will be able to perform using your account.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nIf you are routed to a Twitter website and you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re already logged in to your account, use the Authorize app button to connect the app. If you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re not already logged in to your account, you will need to log in. Before you enter your username and password, check that the page is secure by verifying the URL starts with https://twitter.com. If the page is secure, enter your username and password and use the Sign In button to connect the app.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 5\n          \n\nIf you are routed to the Twitter for Android app, use the Allow or Connect button to connect the app. If you have multiple Twitter accounts on your device, you may need to select the account you wish to connect to the app.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nNote: You can always review and revoke access for apps at any time by visiting the Apps and sessions section of your account settings.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nOn the website of the app you want to connect, find the button/link asking you to connect your Twitter account (usually "Connect to Twitter", "Sign in with Twitter" or something similar). \n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nYou\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll be routed to a Twitter website asking you to authorize the app to use your account. \n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nYou can review the various permissions you are granting to the app. You will see examples of actions the app will be able to perform with your account.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nIf you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re already logged in to your account, use the Authorize app button to connect the app.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 5\n          \n\nIf you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re not already logged in to your account, you will need to log in. Before you enter your username and password, check that the page is secure by verifying the URL starts with https://twitter.com. If the page is secure, enter your username and password and use the Sign In button to connect the app.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 6\n          \n\nYou can review and revoke access for apps connected to your account at any time by visiting the Apps and sessions section of your account settings.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to revoke access or remove an app\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nSign in to your account.\nGo to the Apps and sessions section of your account settings. All of the apps connected to your account will be displayed. You can see the specific permissions that each app has to use your account listed under the app name and description.\nIf you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99d like to disconnect an app from your account, click the Revoke access button next to the app or at the bottom of the page after clicking the app\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s name.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\r\nIf an app asks for your password to access your account\n\r\nIf you wish to grant a third-party app access to your account, we recommend that you only do so using Twitter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s OAuth method. OAuth is a secure connection method and doesn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t require you to give your Twitter username and password to the third party. You should be particularly cautious when you\'re asked to give your username and password to an app or website. When you give your username and password to someone else, they can gain complete control of your account and can lock you out or take actions that cause your account to be suspended.\n\nIf you are unsure about whether a login page for a third-party app is using OAuth, go directly to twitter.com and enter your credentials there, and then navigate back to the app. If the app is using OAuth, the app should not require you to enter your username and password again. You can learn more about how to check that you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re on twitter.com with our account security tips.\n\nIf you previously provided your password to an app that you are now unsure about, revoke its access on the Apps and sessions section of your account settings and change your password.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nNote: You should be especially wary of and never provide your username and password to:\nWebsites claiming to help you \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cget more followers fast!\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d (see our following rules and best practices for more information).Apps which post affiliate ads to your timeline.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nIf you suspect a bad app is still connected to your account\n\r\nImmediately revoke its access on the Apps and sessions section of your account settings and change your password. If you are experiencing problems with an app, please read the compromised accounts article for more information.\n\n\nIf you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re having issues with a third-party app\n\r\nBecause third-party apps are not owned and operated by Twitter, we\'re not able to troubleshoot them. It\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s best to reach out to the app developer for answers to your questions or to let them know about a problem you\'re having with their product.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nAvailable tools\nThird-party tools created by developers add new functionalities and can enhance your Twitter experience. These tools are self-serve, and many are free to use. You can learn more about some of the tools currently available below.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nPlease note: We\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re early in our effort to make third-party tools available and discoverable. Additionally, some tools are created by Twitter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s internal development team. Although some of these tools are only available to specific devices and operating systems, we hope to extend access across all devices and operating systems.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\nTimelines\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          Timelines\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nCustom Timelines are curated feeds. These feeds may be created by third-parties who select and provide content around interests and events, or by Twitter based on general insights. For example, the Popular Videos Timeline created by Twitter, uses similar information to how we select topics to populate and order video content.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nThese custom feeds run parallel to the Home timeline and appear on a separate tab after you add a custom Timeline from a prompt. Easily switch between tabs for more control of your Twitter experience as you deep-dive into the content that interests you most.\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nNote: Content that appears in a custom Timeline is selected and ordered based on relevance to the Timeline\'s theme using information like search terms, Topics, handles, and manual curation.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to add a custom Timeline on twitter.com\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nAfter you see a prompt about a custom Timeline on the Home screen, you can easily add it by following the steps below. For example, if you see a prompt for a Popular Videos Timeline, clicking Add Timeline will create a Popular Videos tab next to your Home timeline tab.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nClick Check it out.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0A prompt appears with information about the Timeline and the third party that curated the content. Click Add Timeline.\n\r\nThis timeline is now pinned next to your Home timeline.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Use the tabs to switch between the Home timeline and the custom\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Timeline.\n\nYou can now navigate through the new Timeline just like you would with your Home timeline.\n\n\n\n\nNote: Right now, you can only add custom Timelines on Twitter for iOS and web.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to remove a custom Timeline from twitter.com\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nIf you ever want to remove a custom Timeline, please follow the steps below:\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nNavigate to the Timeline you want to remove.Look for the settings option below the Composer.\nClick Timelines settings.A prompt appears asking if you want to remove the Timeline. Click Remove Timeline.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0A confirmation prompt appears asking if you really want to remove the Timeline. Click Yes, remove Timeline.\n\nYou\'ll no longer see the custom Timeline on twitter.com.\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nTwitter Toolbox\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          Twitter Toolbox\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWe\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re experimenting with Twitter Toolbox, a hub where you can discover other\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nself-serve, third-party tools created by developers to enhance your Twitter experience.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nTwitter Toolbox currently offers a selection of tools in 3 categories: Expression, Safety, and Measurement.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nExpression tools: Add these to your Twitter account for enhanced creativity.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nSafety tools: This selection of tools offers options for protecting your account from harmful content and profiles.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nMeasurement tools: Get more insights on content performance and trends when you connect these developer tools.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      Getting Started with Twitter Toolbox\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nDiscover and learn more about developer tools available to add to your Twitter account by navigating to the Twitter Toolbox. \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0From there, you can easily add a tool by following the steps below:\n\n\n\n\nSelect the tool you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re interested in adding.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Click Add to Twitter.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Follow the instructions on the third-party website to authenticate and connect the tool with your Twitter account.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nYou should receive instructions on how to use the tool.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to remove a tool you added\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nIf you ever want to remove a tool, please follow the steps below:\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nFrom the main menu, navigate to Settings and privacy.Select Security and account access.\nSelect Apps and sessions.Select the tool you wish to remove.Select\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Revoke app permissions.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nTweet Tiles\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          Tweet Tiles\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nTwitter\'s internal development team is currently experimenting with Tweet Tiles, a way to attach customizable formats to a Tweet.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nRight now, people on iOS and web may see and interact with Tweet Tiles that include text, images, videos, or other elements like a button from people in the initial test group. These formats are designed to easily engage with content and make your timeline more dynamic and visual.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\nWhen someone in our initial test group posts a Tweet Tile, people on iOS and web who are part of this experiment will automatically see the Tweet Tiles they post on the Home timeline. Like Tweet Cards, Tweet Tiles render automatically when you paste a URL.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\nPlease note: Not all followers will automatically see the Tweet Tiles, and if you Retweet a Tweet Tile or share a Tweet Tile URL, others might not be able to see it.\xc3\x82'


=== b'Timelines' ===

b'Third-party apps are applications built on the Twitter platform by external developers, and are not owned or operated by Twitter. When you connect a third-party app to your Twitter account, you are granting that app access to use your account. Depending on its permissions, an authorized app may be able to obtain information from and use your account in various ways, such as reading your Tweets, seeing who you follow, updating your profile, posting Tweets on your behalf, accessing your Direct Messages, or seeing your email address. You can learn more about the specific access in the App permissions\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0section below. Addiontally you can choose to log out of your active Twitter sessions.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\nNote: You should be cautious before giving any third-party app access to your account. If you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re not comfortable with granting an app access to your account, simply click \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9ccancel\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d on the authorization page to decline the app\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s access. We also suggest you regularly review third-party apps which have access to use your account to confirm that you still want to give them access. You can review and revoke access for apps by visiting the Apps and sessions section of your account settings.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nLogging out of active Twitter sessions\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to log out of your active Twitter sessions\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nSign in to your account.\nFrom your\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Settings and privacy, go to the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Apps and sessions\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0section of your account settings. Below\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Sessions, all of the active login sessions connected to your account will be displayed. You can see the location and time of login.\nIf you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99d like to log out of any of the sessions listed, click the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Log out\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0button next to the session, or click\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Log out all other sessions\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0at the top of the list to end all other sessions at once. Please note that while logging out of a session will prevent further actions from that session such as Tweeting, Liking, and replying, it may not delete data (e.g., Direct Messages) that was previously cached on the device while the session was active.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nApp permissions\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\r\n App permissions\n\r\nThird-party apps may request access to perform different actions using your Twitter account.\nOAuth 1.0a User Context\nApps using OAuth 1.0a User Context may ask for the following permissions to access certain information in your account and take certain actions:\nRead\nApps with read access to your Twitter account will have the ability to:\nProfile information: View your profile information, such as your name, location, description, and profile and header photos. Note that the email address associated with your Twitter account and your phone number are not considered profile information. An app will not be able to view your email address unless you grant the app specific permission to do so.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Tweets: View your Tweets (including details such as the number of times a Tweet has been viewed and the interactions others have with a Tweet) and Tweets from accounts you follow on your timeline, including any protected Tweets.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Account settings: View your account settings, such as your preferred language and time zone.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Other accounts: See who you follow, mute, and block.Lists: View your Lists of Twitter accounts.Collections: View your collections of Tweets.\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nOAuth 1.0a User Context\nApps using OAuth 1.0a User Context may ask for the following permissions:\nRead and Write\nApps with read and write access to your Twitter account will have access to view your information as described in the Read section above, and will also have the ability to:\nProfile information: Update your profile information for you.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nTweets: Post Tweets and media on your behalf, delete Tweets for you, and engage with Tweets posted by others for you (for example, like, un-like, or reply to a Tweet, Retweet, etc.).\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nAccount settings: Manage your account settings for you.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nOther accounts: Follow and unfollow accounts for you, and mute, block, or report accounts on your behalf.\nLists: Create Lists of Twitter accounts for you, manage your Lists (for example, add and remove accounts from Lists) for you, and delete your Lists for you.\nCollections: Create collections of Tweets for you, manage your collections (for example, add and remove Tweets from collections) for you, and delete your collections for you.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\nRead, Write, and Direct Messages\nApps with read, write, and Direct Message access to your Twitter account will have access to view your information and take actions as described above in the Read and Write sections, and will also have the ability to: send Direct Messages for you, view Direct Messages you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve sent and received, and manage and delete your Direct Messages. Remember that each communication participant has their own copy of the communication \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x94 deletion of a Direct Message will remove it from your account, not the accounts of the other participants to the communication.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nEmail Address\nIn addition to the permissions above, apps may also ask for permission to view the email address associated with your Twitter account.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nTwitter Ads\nIf you use Twitter Ads, apps may also ask to:\nAnalytics: Access your advertising data, including your campaigns, audiences, business and ad account information (such as account name, ID, and creation date, business name, timezone, and users), ad account and user settings (such as notification email, contact phone number and extensions, industry type, email subscription settings, and tax settings), and creatives and media.\nCampaign and account management: Access your advertising data as described above, create and manage your advertising data (such as media, creatives, campaigns, and audiences) for you, and manage your account (such as account name, industry type, account and user settings, etc.).\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\nLearn more about granting access to your Twitter Ads account with multi-user login.\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nOAuth 2.0 User Context\nOAuth 2.0 User Context enables a developer to set more granular access for their app. Apps using OAuth 2.0 User Context may may ask for permissions in the following categories:\nRead\nRead permissions define what an app can see in your Twitter account. For example, an app may ask permission to view things like:\nAll the Tweets and Spaces you can view, including Tweets from protected accounts.People who follow you and people you follow.Accounts you\'ve muted and blocked.\nYou\'ll see a list of things an app is requesting permission to view under "Things this App can view."\nWrite\nWrite permissions define what actions an app can take on your behalf. For example, an app may ask permission to do things like:\nTweet and retweet for you.Hide and unhide replies to your Tweets.Follow and unfollow people for you.\nYou\'ll see a list of things an app is requesting permission to do on your behalf under "Things this App can do."\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWe do not share your Twitter password with apps. Remember that when you authorize an app to access your Twitter account or take actions on your behalf, the app may use, store, and share your information in accordance with its own business practices. While app developers agree to abide by our rules and guidelines, we strongly recommend that you review an app\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s terms and privacy policy before you authorize the app to access your account.\nLearn more about our rules and guidelines for third-party app developers in our Developer Policy.\r\n\xc3\x82'

If the page is secure, enter your username and password and use the Sign In button to connect the app.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 5\n          \n\nIf you are routed to the Twitter for Android app, use the Allow or Connect button to connect the app. If you have multiple Twitter accounts on your device, you may need to select the account you wish to connect to the app.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nNote: You can always review and revoke access for apps at any time by visiting the Apps and sessions section of your account settings.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nOn the website of the app you want to connect, find the button/link asking you to connect your Twitter account (usually "Connect to Twitter", "Sign in with Twitter" or something similar). \n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nYou\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll be routed to a Twitter website asking you to authorize the app to use your account. \n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nYou can review the various permissions you are granting to the app. You will see examples of actions the app will be able to perform with your account.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nIf you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re already logged in to your account, use the Authorize app button to connect the app.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 5\n          \n\nIf you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re not already logged in to your account, you will need to log in. Before you enter your username and password, check that the page is secure by verifying the URL starts with https://twitter.com. If the page is secure, enter your username and password and use the Sign In button to connect the app.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 6\n          \n\nYou can review and revoke access for apps connected to your account at any time by visiting the Apps and sessions section of your account settings.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to revoke access or remove an app\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nSign in to your account.\nGo to the Apps and sessions section of your account settings. All of the apps connected to your account will be displayed. You can see the specific permissions that each app has to use your account listed under the app name and description.\nIf you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99d like to disconnect an app from your account, click the Revoke access button next to the app or at the bottom of the page after clicking the app\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s name.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\r\nIf an app asks for your password to access your account\n\r\nIf you wish to grant a third-party app access to your account, we recommend that you only do so using Twitter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s OAuth method. OAuth is a secure connection method and doesn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t require you to give your Twitter username and password to the third party. You should be particularly cautious when you\'re asked to give your username and password to an app or website. When you give your username and password to someone else, they can gain complete control of your account and can lock you out or take actions that cause your account to be suspended.\n\nIf you are unsure about whether a login page for a third-party app is using OAuth, go directly to twitter.com and enter your credentials there, and then navigate back to the app. If the app is using OAuth, the app should not require you to enter your username and password again. You can learn more about how to check that you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re on twitter.com with our account security tips.\n\nIf you previously provided your password to an app that you are now unsure about, revoke its access on the Apps and sessions section of your account settings and change your password.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nNote: You should be especially wary of and never provide your username and password to:\nWebsites claiming to help you \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cget more followers fast!\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d (see our following rules and best practices for more information).Apps which post affiliate ads to your timeline.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nIf you suspect a bad app is still connected to your account\n\r\nImmediately revoke its access on the Apps and sessions section of your account settings and change your password. If you are experiencing problems with an app, please read the compromised accounts article for more information.\n\n\nIf you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re having issues with a third-party app\n\r\nBecause third-party apps are not owned and operated by Twitter, we\'re not able to troubleshoot them. It\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s best to reach out to the app developer for answers to your questions or to let them know about a problem you\'re having with their product.'


=== b'Timelines' ===

b"Timelines\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nCustom Timelines are curated feeds. These feeds may be created by third-parties who select and provide content around interests and events, or by Twitter based on general insights. For example, the Popular Videos Timeline created by Twitter, uses similar information to how we select topics to populate and order video content.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nThese custom feeds run parallel to the Home timeline and appear on a separate tab after you add a custom Timeline from a prompt. Easily switch between tabs for more control of your Twitter experience as you deep-dive into the content that interests you most.\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nNote: Content that appears in a custom Timeline is selected and ordered based on relevance to the Timeline's theme using information like search terms, Topics, handles, and manual curation.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to add a custom Timeline on twitter.com\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nAfter you see a prompt about a custom Timeline on the Home screen, you can easily add it by following the steps below. For example, if you see a prompt for a Popular Videos Timeline, clicking Add Timeline will create a Popular Videos tab next to your Home timeline tab.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nClick Check it out.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0A prompt appears with information about the Timeline and the third party that curated the content. Click Add Timeline.\n\r\nThis timeline is now pinned next to your Home timeline.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Use the tabs to switch between the Home timeline and the custom\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Timeline.\n\nYou can now navigate through the new Timeline just like you would with your Home timeline.\n\n\n\n\nNote: Right now, you can only add custom Timelines on Twitter for iOS and web.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to remove a custom Timeline from twitter.com\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nIf you ever want to remove a custom Timeline, please follow the steps below:\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nNavigate to the Timeline you want to remove.Look for the settings option below the Composer.\nClick Timelines settings.A prompt appears asking if you want to remove the Timeline. Click Remove Timeline.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0A confirmation prompt appears asking if you really want to remove the Timeline. Click Yes, remove Timeline.\n\nYou'll no longer see the custom Timeline on twitter.com.\n\xc3\x82"

b'Twitter Toolbox\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWe\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re experimenting with Twitter Toolbox, a hub where you can discover other\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nself-serve, third-party tools created by developers to enhance your Twitter experience.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nTwitter Toolbox currently offers a selection of tools in 3 categories: Expression, Safety, and Measurement.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nExpression tools: Add these to your Twitter account for enhanced creativity.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nSafety tools: This selection of tools offers options for protecting your account from harmful content and profiles.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nMeasurement tools: Get more insights on content performance and trends when you connect these developer tools.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      Getting Started with Twitter Toolbox\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nDiscover and learn more about developer tools available to add to your Twitter account by navigating to the Twitter Toolbox. \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0From there, you can easily add a tool by following the steps below:\n\n\n\n\nSelect the tool you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re interested in adding.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Click Add to Twitter.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Follow the instructions on the third-party website to authenticate and connect the tool with your Twitter account.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nYou should receive instructions on how to use the tool.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to remove a tool you added\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nIf you ever want to remove a tool, please follow the steps below:\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nFrom the main menu, navigate to Settings and privacy.Select Security and account access.\nSelect Apps and sessions.Select the tool you wish to remove.Select\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Revoke app permissions.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82'


=== b'Timelines' ===

b"Tweet Tiles\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nTwitter's internal development team is currently experimenting with Tweet Tiles, a way to attach customizable formats to a Tweet.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nRight now, people on iOS and web may see and interact with Tweet Tiles that include text, images, videos, or other elements like a button from people in the initial test group. These formats are designed to easily engage with content and make your timeline more dynamic and visual.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\nWhen someone in our initial test group posts a Tweet Tile, people on iOS and web who are part of this experiment will automatically see the Tweet Tiles they post on the Home timeline. Like Tweet Cards, Tweet Tiles render automatically when you paste a URL.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\nPlease note: Not all followers will automatically see the Tweet Tiles, and if you Retweet a Tweet Tile or share a Tweet Tile URL, others might not be able to see it.\xc3\x82"


=== b'What is the Tweet activity dashboard?' ===

b'What is the Tweet activity dashboard?\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nThe Tweet activity dashboard is a tool you can use to learn more about your Tweets and how they resonate with your audience.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nUse the activity dashboard to:\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nSee how people engage with your Tweets in real time.Compare your Tweet activity and followers, and see how they trend over time.Click on any Tweet to get a detailed view of the number of Retweets, replies, likes, follows, or clicks it receives.Get detailed insights into who your audience is, especially those who engage with your Tweets.Download your Tweet metrics.\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nTo get started accessing your Tweet activity, log in to analytics.twitter.com with your Twitter username and password.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to access the dashboard\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nFrom the Twitter for iOS app: \nMake sure you have installed the latest version of Twitter for iPhone or iPad.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Tap the analytics icon visible in your Tweets.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nThe Tweet activity dashboard is available to users who primarily Tweet in Arabic, Brazilian Portuguese, Danish, Dutch, English, Filipino, Finnish, French, German, Indonesian, Italian, Japanese, Korean, Norwegian, Russian, Simplified Chinese, Spanish, Swedish, Thai, Traditional Chinese, Turkish, and have had an account for at least 14 days. We\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re working to roll this out to everyone soon.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nFrom the Twitter for Android app:\nMake sure you have installed the latest version of Twitter for Android.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Tap the analytics icon visible in your Tweets.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nThe Tweet activity dashboard is available to users who primarily Tweet in Arabic, Brazilian Portuguese, Danish, Dutch, English, Filipino, Finnish, French, German, Indonesian, Italian, Japanese, Korean, Norwegian, Russian, Simplified Chinese, Spanish, Swedish, Thai, Traditional Chinese, Turkish, and have had an account for at least 14 days. We\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re working to roll this out to everyone soon.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nOn a desktop or laptop computer, visit analytics.twitter.com and click on Tweets.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nThe Tweet activity dashboard is available to users who primarily Tweet in Arabic, Brazilian Portuguese, Danish, Dutch, English, Filipino, Finnish, French, German, Indonesian, Italian, Japanese, Korean, Norwegian, Russian, Simplified Chinese, Spanish, Swedish, Thai, Traditional Chinese, Turkish, and have had an account for at least 14 days. We\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re working to roll this out to everyone soon.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          How to use the dashbaord\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nClick into an individual Tweet to see specific data for that Tweet:\n\n\n\n\n\n\nDesktop\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nMobile\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nAvailable on Twitter for iPhone and Twitter for Android app.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Tap the Tweet to view the Tweet detail page, and then tap View Tweet activity.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nAccount summary metrics:\nTweets: Number of times you Tweeted\nTweet impressions: Number of times users are served your Tweet in timeline, search results, or from your profileProfile visits: Number of times users visited your profile pageMentions: Number of times your @username was mentioned in TweetsNew followers: Number of new followers you gainedTweets linking to you: Number of times your Twitter Card(s) was Tweeted by you and/or other people\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nMonthly highlights:\n\nTop Tweet: Tweet that received the highest number of impressions\nTop media Tweet: Tweet with photo, video, or Vine that received the highest number of impressionsTop Card Tweet: Tweet with a Twitter Card that received the highest number of impressions; this can include other people\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s TweetsTop mention: Tweet that mentioned your @handle and received the highest number of impressions; this can include other people\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s TweetsTop follower: Account with the highest follower count that followed you in a given month\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nYou can select the View Tweet details button to learn more information about a specific Tweet or select View follower to find out more about your top follower.\n\n\n\n\nFAQs\n\n\n\n\nHow up-to-date is account home?\n\nSummary metrics reported in account home are updated once every 24 hours, through the previous day. Information about a particular Tweet from the Tweet activity dashboard is updated in real-time.\n\n\n\n\n\nHow far back does account home report results?\n\nSeptember 2014 or when your account first accessed Twitter Analytics, whichever is more recent.\n\n\n\n\n\nHow can I use account home to improve my content or account strategy?\n\nYou can use the information in account home to quickly identify your top Tweets to promote to a wider audience, engage with your most influential followers, or as a starting point to dive deeper into your account or Tweet performance. For example, you may want to review your Top Tweets, and share more of the content that your followers are already engaging with.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          Share this article\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nTweet'
