=== b'How to use TweetDeck' ===

b"Getting started with TweetDeck\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Getting started with TweetDeck\n          \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to start using TweetDeck\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nGo to http://tweetdeck.twitter.com, or open the desktop app for Mac.Log in with your Twitter account. We recommend that you use a Twitter account that is not shared with other individuals.Once you're logged in, you can connect multiple Twitter accounts to your TweetDeck account.\n\n\n\n\nNote:\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0If you are using an old version of our desktop app for Mac (older than Mac: 3.5.0), you will not be able to sign in with a Twitter account or create a new account until you upgrade to the latest version.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\r\nIf you use TweetDeck in a corporate or team environment, learn how to\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0set up a team account.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to connect multiple Twitter accounts in your TweetDeck\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nClick Accounts\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0in the navigation bar.\nClick on Link another account you own.Read the message to understand that you'll be creating a team relationship account you're adding, then click continue.In the new window, enter the username or email and password of the account and click Authorize.You\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re ready to use TweetDeck!\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      How to remove an account from TweetDeck\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nClick Accounts in the navigation bar.Expand the account you wish to delete by clicking the down arrow.Click Leave team and confirm by clicking Leave.\n\n\n\n\nNote:\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0The account you are signed into TweetDeck with cannot be removed from TweetDeck.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\r\n Managing multiple accounts on TweetDeck\n\r\nSelect a default account:\nYou can select which of your accounts to use as your default account. This is the account you will compose a Tweet from, like a Tweet from, and reply to Tweets with.\nClick Accounts in the navigation bar.Expand the account you wish to set as the default by clicking the down arrow.Toggle on the Default account option.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nTweeting from multiple accounts:\nTweetDeck allows you to easily Tweet from multiple accounts. To select which accounts you would like to Tweet from:\nClick on the Tweet button at the top of the navigation bar; the accounts you have authorized will be listed at the top (you can hover over an icon to see the username of the account).Select which account you would like to Tweet from (if the account is selected, it will be highlighted with a green checkmark).\nTip: Schedule Tweets\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0(with or without an asset) in advance for any account connected to your TweetDeck.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nLiking from multiple accounts:\nTweetDeck allows you to like a Tweet from multiple accounts.\nClick on the more icon\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n on the Tweet.From the menu that pops up, click on Like from accounts\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\xa6Click Like next to the account(s) you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99d like to like from.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nFollowing from multiple accounts:\nTweetDeck allows you to follow someone from multiple accounts. You can also follow someone by clicking follow on their profile, but only your default account will follow them.\nClick on the account that you wish to follow; a profile will appear.Click on the more icon \n\n\n and then select Follow from accounts...Choose which accounts you would like to follow from.\nNote: The same instructions apply when unfollowing an account.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWhy is it more secure to log in with a personal Twitter username?\n\r\nIf you log in using a personal username that only you have the password for, you can safely access your team accounts without any risk to account security. We recommend that you use login verification for added security.\n\n\nHow to create a Tweet in TweetDeck\n\r\nThe Tweet Composer in TweetDeck makes it easy to join the conversation, whether you want to share what\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s happening with words, images, or video.\nClick Tweet\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0while logged into your Twitter account.If you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re logged into multiple accounts, confirm the Twitter account you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99d like to Tweet from is selected.\nCompose your Tweet with text. Include an image or video by selecting\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0the \n\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Add images or video button.\nClick Tweet to share.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nUsing TweetDeck columns\n\r\nInstead of a single timeline, TweetDeck allows you to add columns to display specific content that interests you and view them side by side. Add columns that show all your mentions, the results of a search query, a list of likes, the latest Tweets from a hashtag or trend, etc.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nTo add a column:\nFrom the navigation bar, click on the plus icon  to select Add column.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Select the type of column you would like to add.Under Your accounts, select the account you wish to populate the column.\n\n\n\n\nNote:\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0You can also create columns using information based on actions from other accounts. Click on the account username and choose from actions such as their mentions, lists, collections, or likes.\n\n\n\n\nTo remove a column:\nClick the filter icon\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0 in the column header, next to the column title.Click the Remove button to delete a column.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nColumn filters:\nYou can easily control the type of Tweets you would like displayed in each of your columns. You can select from Content, Location,\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Users, Engagements or Alerts; or a combination of the three.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nContent filtering allows you to filter the column by a certain type of Tweet, such as Retweets, Tweets containing a specific word or phrase, or Tweets with photos.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0The location filter allows you to filter for Tweets geotagged in specific locations.The user filter allows you to filter Tweets within a specific column written by a certain author and those they mention.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0The engagement filter allows you to filter Tweets with a minimum number of Retweets, likes or replies.The alert filter allows you to enable pop-ups or sounds for a particular column.Note: If you create a search column, you can also filter results by location, date, and engagement. The location filter allows you to easily narrow down your search results to find relevant content in the area you are interested in. Only unprotected Tweets geotagged with a location will appear in search results when a location filter is applied.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nTo create a filter:\nClick the filter icon\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0 in the column header, next to the column title.Select which types of filter(s) (Content, Users, or Alerts) you would like applied to the column.Click the filter icon\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n again to collapse the column settings.\nNote: Columns with custom filtering will display Filtered by along with the icon for the filter you have enabled.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nColumn reordering:\nEasily rearrange the order of columns in TweetDeck with just a few quick clicks.\nClick the filter icon\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0 in the column header, next to the column title.Click the left or right arrow depending on which direction you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99d like to move the column.\nNote: You can also drag and drop the columns by their corresponding icons from the navigation bar to reorder your columns.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nTypes of TweetDeck columns and what they display\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nHome: Home timeline for any specific account.User: Tweets from a specific account.Notifications: Notifications for a specific account, including when the account's Tweets. are Retweeted, liked, or mentioned, and when someone follows the account.Search: A specific search term.Lists: Create or connect a list you already follow.Collection: A timeline of curated Tweets, hand-selected by you, to share with others.Activity: What\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s happening with the accounts you follow.Likes: Tweets marked as likes from a specific account.Messages (one account): Direct Messages for a specific account.Mentions (one account): When someone mentions a specific account.Followers: Follow activity for a specific account.Scheduled: Your scheduled Tweets.Messages (all accounts): Direct Messages from all your authorized accounts in aggregate.Mentions (all accounts): Mentions from all accounts.Trending: Specific worldwide trends.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          Share this article\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nTweet"

=== b'Getting started with Subscriptions' ===

b"Subscriptions\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0can help people on Twitter earn monthly income from the content they create. Subscriptions purchases are currently available globally on Twitter for iOS and Android, as well as on twitter.com in the US, Canada, New Zealand, and Australia. What should I do?\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nGetting paid\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWho sets the price of Subscriptions?\nWhat if I want to change the subscription price Twitter charges for my Subscriptions offering?\nHow much revenue can I earn?\nHow will I get paid?\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWhen can I get a payout?\n\nI\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve met the minimum payment amount. === b'FAQ' ===

b"Tips and tipping\n        \n\n          FAQ\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat is Tips?\n\nTips is a feature that lets you add links to select third-party payment services to your Twitter profile. When you turn on Tips on your profile, people can support you by tapping on your Tips\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon to send you money or Bitcoin off-platform via the third-party payment services and platforms you have added.\n\n\n\n\n\nWhy is Twitter introducing Tips?\n\nPeople on Twitter already share their Venmo handle and $Cashtag in Tweets. And people are often informed, entertained, and even moved by conversations taking place on the Home timeline and in\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Twitter Spaces. With Tips, we're creating an easy way to direct people to links to your payment profiles and we\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re making it easier to support the people driving the conversation on Twitter \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93 whether you want to support a content creator, help someone fundraise, tip someone who just needs some help or thank someone for making you laugh.\n\n\n\n\n\nWhere is Tips available?\n\nFor people on iOS and Android, you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll see the money \n\n\n\n icon on the profile pages of people who have set up Tips on their profile.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0For people on Android, you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll also find it on their profile while in Twitter Spaces.\nNote: Currently Tips is not available on web.\n\n\n\n\n\nHow do I set up my Tips?\n\nOn iOS or Android, go to Edit Profile. Then tap Tips, which is off by default. You will be required to consent to our General Tipping policy to turn on Tips on your profile.\nOnce you have agreed to our General Tipping policy, you will be brought to the Tips settings screen. Toggle Allow tips to on and then choose the third-party service(s) you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99d like to use. Add in your third-party service username(s). You will need to have at least one username entered for your Tips\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon to appear on your Twitter profile.\nWhen you add a third-party payment service to your profile, please note that your username on that service will be publicly linked to your Twitter account. Information about you, including, but not limited to, your full name, address and your tip may be shared with the recipient or others, subject to the terms of the third-party payment service. Please review each service\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s terms for more details.\n\n\n\n\n\nWho can send and receive Tips and what can I use Tips for?\n\nYou must be at least 18 years old to request, receive, or send tips via Tips or anywhere on our platform.\nYou can tip to show support, show appreciation, help out or reward anyone you want \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93 from emerging creators and journalists to Twitter Spaces hosts and more. Because tipping occurs through third-party payment services, you must also ensure that your tips comply with the terms and policies of those services.\nPlease see our\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0General Tipping policy to learn more about who can request or give tips and for what. Our\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0General Tipping policy applies to all tipping on Twitter, whether via our Tips feature or otherwise.\nSending someone a tip does not entitle you to any premium or exclusive content from them,\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0nor does it replace\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0purchasing a Subscription. To find out more about Subscriptions, please see our Subscriptions policy.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\nIf I send a Tip, what percentage will the person receive?\n\nTips in the form of money and Bitcoin are sent off Twitter via third-party payment services. Twitter will not receive any portion of these payments, but the third-party payment services may charge fees.\n\n\n\n\n\nHow do I send someone a tip?\n\nYou can tip people using the Tips\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n icon if they have toggled the feature on and added their usernames from third-party payment processors.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0On both iOS and Android you will find the Tips feature on the main Twitter profile under the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0On Android you will also find the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon when you tap on the profile of someone inside of Twitter Spaces.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWhen you tap to send the tip, we will link you off of the Twitter platform to the app or website of the third-party payment service you selected. Your tip and activity on that service will be subject to the third-party payment service\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s terms.\nWhen you send Bitcoin through Strike, you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll be able to switch between seeing the currency in Satoshi (Sats) or BTC.\nThrough Tips, you'll also be able to copy someone's Bitcoin or Ethereum address and paste their address into whatever wallet you use.\nYou will be able to send tips from your account on the third-party service and recipients will be able to see your username on that service. Information about you, including, but not limited to, your full name, address and your tip may be shared with the recipient or others, subject to the terms of the third-party payment service. Please review each service\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s terms for more details.\n\n\n\n\n\nHow do I choose a payment provider for tipping?\n\nWhen you set up, or add additional third-party service(s) to, through your Tips settings, you may only choose from the select third-party service(s) listed in your Tips settings. Twitter reserves the right, in our discretion, to add, modify, or remove the specific third-party service(s) (in any given country) that are available to link to Tips.\n\n\n\n\n\nIs there a dollar limit on how much you can tip? \n\nTwitter does not impose limits on the amount you can tip; however, third-party payment platforms, subject to their terms of service, may impose limits on the amount you can tip."


=== b'FAQ' ===

=== b'How to use Spaces' ===

b'Note: Anyone can join, listen, and speak in a Space on Twitter for iOS and Android.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Currently you can listen in a Space on web. We are working on building out more functionality on twitter.com.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      Quick links\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nHow to use Spaces\nSpaces FAQ\nSpaces Feedback Community\nCommunity Spaces\nWhat Spaces will feel like\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          How to use Spaces\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      How do you start a Space?\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nThe creator of a Space is the host. As a host on iOS, you can start a Space by long pressing on the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Tweet Composer\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n from your Home timeline and and then selecting the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Spaces\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon.\nYou can also start a Space by selecting the Spaces tab on the bottom of your timeline.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nSpaces are public, so anyone can join as a listener, including people who don\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t follow you. Listeners can be directly invited into a Space by DMing them a link to the Space, Tweeting out a link, or sharing a link elsewhere.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nUp to 13 people (including the host\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0and 2 co-hosts) can speak in a Space at any given time.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0When creating a new Space, you will see options to\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Name your Space\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0and\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Start your Space.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nTo schedule a Space, select\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Schedule for later. Choose the date and time you\'d like your Space to go live.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 5\n          \n\nOnce the Space has started, the host can send requests to listeners to become co-hosts or speakers by selecting the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0people\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n and adding co-hosts or speakers, or selecting a person\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s profile picture within a Space and adding them as a co-host or speaker.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Listeners can request permission to speak from the host by selecting the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Request\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon below the microphone.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 6\n          \n\nWhen creating a Space,\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0the host will join with their mic off and be the only speaker in the Space. When ready, select\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Start your Space.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 7\n          \n\nAllow mic access (speaking ability) to speakers by toggling\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Allow mic access\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0to on.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 8\n          \n\nAs the host, your Space will automatically serve live captions.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 9\n          \n\nAs a listener, choose whether or not you want to see captions by selecting the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Show captions\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0button in your Spaces settings.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 10\n          \n\nGet started chatting in your Space.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 11\n          \n\nAs a host,\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0make sure to Tweet out the link to your Space so other people can join. Select the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon to\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Share via a Tweet.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nThe creator of a Space is the host. As a host on\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Android, you can start a Space by long pressing the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Tweet Composer\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0on your Home timeline and selecting the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Spaces\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n icon.\nYou can also start a Space by selecting the Spaces tab on the bottom of your timeline.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nSpaces are public, so anyone can join as a listener, including people who don\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t follow you. Listeners can be directly invited into a Space by DMing them a link to the Space, Tweeting out a link, or sharing a link elsewhere.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nUp to 13 people (including the host\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0and 2 co-hosts) can speak in a Space at any given time.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0When creating a new Space, you will see options to\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Name your Space\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0and\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Start your Space.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nTo schedule a Space, select\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Schedule for later. Choose the date and time you\'d like your Space to go live.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 5\n          \n\nOnce the Space has started, the host can send requests to listeners to become co-hosts or speakers by selecting the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0people\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n and adding co-hosts or speakers, or selecting a person\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s profile picture within a Space and adding them as a co-host or speaker.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Listeners can request permission to speak from the host by selecting the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Request\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon below the microphone.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 6\n          \n\nWhen creating a Space,\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0the host will join with their mic off and be the only speaker in the Space. When ready, select\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Start your Space.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 7\n          \n\nAllow mic access (speaking ability) to speakers by toggling\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Allow mic access\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0to on.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 8\n          \n\nAs the host, your Space will automatically serve live captions.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 9\n          \n\nAs a listener, choose whether or not you want to see captions by selecting the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Show captions\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0button in your Spaces settings.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 10\n          \n\nGet started chatting in your Space.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 11\n          \n\nAs a host,\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0make sure to Tweet out the link to your Space so other people can join. Select the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon to\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Share via a Tweet.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          Spaces FAQ\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWhere is Spaces available?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nAnyone can join, listen, and speak in a Space on Twitter for iOS and Android.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Currently, starting a Space on web is not possible, but anyone can join and listen in a Space.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWho can start a Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nPeople on Twitter for iOS and Android can start a Space.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWho can see my Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nFor now, all Spaces are public like Tweets, which means they can be accessed by anyone. They will automatically appear at the top of your Home timeline, and each Space has a link that can be shared publicly.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Since Spaces are publicly accessible by anyone, it may be possible for people to listen to a Space without being listed as a guest in the Space.\nWe make certain information about Spaces available through the Twitter Developer Platform, such as the title of a Space, the hosts and speakers, and whether it is scheduled, in progress, or complete. For a more detailed list of the information about Spaces we make available via the Twitter API, check out our Spaces endpoints documentation.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nCan other people see my presence while I am listening or speaking in a Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nSince all Spaces are public, your presence and activity in a Space is also public. If you are logged into your Twitter account when you are in a Space, you will be visible to everyone in the Space as well as to others, including people who follow you, people who peek into the Space without entering, and developers accessing information about the Space using the Twitter API.\nIf you are listening in a Space, your profile icon will appear with a purple pill at the top of your followers\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 Home timelines. You have the option to change this in your settings.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      Manage who can see your Spaces listening activity\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nSelect your profile photo on the top left menu and navigate to\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Settings and privacy.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nUnder Settings, go to Privacy and safety and then to Spaces.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nChoose if you want to Allow followers to see which Spaces you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re listening to by toggling this on or off.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nSelect your profile photo on the top left menu and navigate to\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Settings and privacy.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nUnder Settings, go to Privacy and safety and then to Spaces.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nChoose if you want to Allow followers to see which Spaces you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re listening to by toggling this on or off.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nOn the left nav menu, select the more\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon and go to Settings and privacy.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nUnder Settings, navigate to Privacy and safety.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nUnder Your Twitter activity, go to Spaces.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nChoose if you want to Allow followers to see which Spaces you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re listening to by toggling this on or off.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nYour followers will always see at the top of their Home timelines what Spaces you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re speaking in.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat does it mean that Spaces are public? Can anyone listen in a Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nSpaces can be listened to by anyone on the Internet. This is part of a broader feature of Spaces that lets anyone listen to Spaces regardless of whether or not they are logged in to a Twitter account (or even have a Twitter account). Because of this, listener counts may not match the actual number of listeners, nor will the profile photos of all listeners necessarily be displayed in a Space.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHow do I invite people to join a Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nInvite people to join a Space by sending an invite via DM, Tweeting the link out to your Home timeline, or copying the invite link to send it out.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWho can join my Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nFor now, all Spaces are public and anyone can join any Space as a listener. If the listener has a user account, you can block their account. If you create a Space or are a speaker in a Space, your followers will see it at the top of their timeline.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWho can speak in my Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nBy default, your Space will always be set to\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Only people you invite to speak. You can also modify the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Speaker permissions\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0once your Space has been created. Select the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n icon, then select\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Adjust settings\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0to see the options for speaker permissions, which include\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Everyone,\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0People you follow, and the default\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Only people you invite to speak. These permissions are only saved for this particular Space, so any Space you create in the future will use the default setting.\nOnce your Space has started, you can send requests to listeners to become speakers\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0or co-hosts by selecting the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n icon and adding speakers or selecting a person\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s profile picture within a Space and adding them as a co-host or speaker. Listeners can request to speak from the host.\nHosts can also invite other people outside of the Space to speak via DM.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHow does co-hosting work?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nUp to 2 people can become co-hosts and speak in a Space in addition to the 11 speakers (including the primary host) at one time. Co-host status can be lost if the co-host leaves the Space. A co-host can remove their own co-host status to become a Listener again.\nHosts can transfer primary admin rights to another co-host. If the original host drops from Space, the first co-host added will become the primary admin.\nOnce a co-host is added to a Space, any accounts they\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve blocked on Twitter who are in the Space will be removed from the Space.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nCan I schedule a Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHosts can schedule a Space up to 30 days in advance and up to 10 scheduled Spaces. Hosts can still create impromptu Spaces in the meantime, and those won\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t count toward the maximum 10 scheduled Spaces.\nBefore you create your Space, select the scheduler\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon and pick the date and time you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99d like to schedule your Space to go live. As your scheduled start time approaches, you will receive push and in-app notifications reminding you to start your Space on time.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0If you don\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t have notifications turned on, follow the in-app steps on About notifications on mobile devices to enable them for Spaces. Scheduled Spaces are public and people can set reminders to be notified when your scheduled Space begins.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHow do I edit my scheduled Space(s)?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nFollow the steps below to edit any of your scheduled Spaces.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      Manage your scheduled Spaces\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nFrom your timeline, navigate to and long press on the \n\n\n. Or, navigate to the Spaces Tab \n\n\n\n\n\n\n at the bottom of your timeline.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nSelect the Spaces \n\n\n\n icon.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nTo manage your scheduled Spaces,\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0select the scheduler\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n icon at the top.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nYou\'ll see the Spaces that you have scheduled.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 5\n          \n\nNavigate to the more\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n icon of the Space you want to manage. You can edit, share, or cancel the Space.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nIf you are editing your Space, make sure to select "Save changes" after making edits.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nFrom your timeline, navigate to the Tweet composer \n\n\n. Or, navigate to the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0 Spaces Tab\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n at the bottom of your timeline.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nSelect the Spaces \n\n\n\n icon.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nTo manage your scheduled Spaces,\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0select the scheduler \n\n\n\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0icon at the top.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nYou\'ll see the Spaces that you have scheduled.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 5\n          \n\nNavigate to the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0more\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n icon of the Space you want to manage. You can edit, share, or cancel the Space.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nIf you are editing your Space, make sure to select "Save changes" after making edits.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHow do I get notified about a scheduled Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nGuests can sign up for reminder notifications from a scheduled Space card in a Tweet. When the host starts the scheduled Space, the interested guests get notified via push and in-app notifications.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nCan I record a Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHosts can record Spaces they create for replay. When creating a Space, toggle on Record Space.\nWhile recording, a recording symbol will appear at the top to indicate that the Space is being recorded by the host. Once the Space ends, you will see how many people attended the Space along with a link to share out via a Tweet. Under Notifications, you can also View details to Tweet the recording. Under host settings, you will have the option to choose where to start your recording with Edit start time. This allows you to cut out any dead air time that might occur at the beginning of a Space.\nIf you choose to record your Space, once the live Space ends, your recording will be immediately and publicly available for anyone to listen to whenever they want. You can always end a recording to make it no longer publicly available on Twitter by deleting your recording via the more \n\n\n icon on the recording itself. Unless you delete your recording, it will remain available for replay after the live Space has ended.* As with live Spaces, Twitter will retain audio copies for 30 after they end to review for violations of the Twitter Rules. If a violation is found, Twitter may retain audio copies for up to 120 days in total. For more information on downloading Spaces, please see below FAQ, "What happens after a Space ends and is the data retained anywhere?"\nCo-hosts and speakers who enter a Space that is being recorded will see a recording symbol (REC). Listeners will also see the recording symbol, but they will not be visible in the recording.\nRecordings will show the host, co-host(s), and speakers from the live Space.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n*Note: Hosts on iOS 9.15+ and Android 9.46+ will be able to record Spaces that last indefinitely. For hosts on older app versions, recording will only be available for 30 days.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0For Spaces that are recorded indefinitely, Twitter will retain a copy for as long as the Space is replayable on Twitter, but for no less than 30 days after the live Space ended.\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat is clipping?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nClipping is a new feature we\'re currently testing and gradually rolling out that lets a limited group of hosts, speakers, and listeners capture 30 seconds of audio from any live or recorded Space and share it through a Tweet if the host has not disabled the clipping function. To start clipping a Space, follow the instructions below to capture the prior 30 seconds of audio from that Space. There is no limit to the number of clips that participants in a Space can create.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWhen you enter the Space as a co-host or speaker, you will be informed that the Space is clippable through a tool tip notification above the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0clipping\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n icon.\n\nNote:\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Currently, creating a clip is available only on iOS and Android, while playing a clip is available on all platforms to everyone.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      Host instructions: How to turn off clipping\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWhen you start your Space, you\'ll receive a notification about what a clip is and how to turn it off, as clipping is on by default. You can turn off clipping at any time. To turn it off, follow the instructions below.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Navigate to the more\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n icon.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nSelect\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Adjust settings \n\n\n\n.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nUnder Clips, toggle Allow clips off.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      Host and speaker instructions: How to create a clipping\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nIn a recorded or live Space that is recorded, navigate to the clipping \n\n\n icon. Please note that, for live Spaces, unless the clipping function is disabled, clips will be publicly available on your Twitter profile after your live Space has ended even though the Space itself will no longer be available.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nOn the Create clip pop-up, go to Next.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nPreview the Tweet and add a comment if you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99d like, similarly to a Quote Tweet.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nSelect\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Tweet to post it to your timeline.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWhy is my clip not displaying captions?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nIf captions weren\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t created for your clip, the reason(s) could include at least one of the following:\nNo one said anythingNo spoken English was detectedLanguage other than English was spokenMusic was playingInaudibleTranscription service couldn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t generate captions\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat controls do hosts have over existing clips?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nAs a host, if you turn off clipping for all Spaces from the onset, no one will be able to clip your Spaces. If you choose to turn off clipping at any point thereafter, the feature will be unavailable moving forward. To delete clips of recorded Spaces made prior to turning off the feature, you will need to delete your Space entirely.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat controls do clip creators have over clips they\'ve created?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nAnyone who creates a clip can delete the clip by deleting the associated Tweet.\nTo delete a Tweet with a clip, navigate to the more\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n icon and select Delete Tweet. For more information, read\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0How to delete a Tweet.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nOther controls over clips: how to report, block, or mute\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nIf you think a clip violates the Twitter Rules, you can report it. On the Tweet with the clip, go to the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0more\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n icon and select Report this Tweet. Learn more about reporting a Tweet.\nYou also have the option to block or mute the account that Tweeted the clip. Navigate to the account\'s profile photo and from the more\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n icon, select the appropriate action.\nSee below FAQs for more information on the controls you have over your Space, blocking, and muting an account, and reporting an account or Space.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat controls do I have over my Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nThe host and co-host(s) of a Space have control over who can speak. They can mute any Speaker, but it is up to the individual to unmute themselves if they receive speaking privileges. Hosts and co-hosts can also remove,\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0report, and\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0block\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0others\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0in the Space.\nSpeakers and listeners can report and block others in the Space, or can report the Space. If you block a participant in the Space, you will also block that person\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s account on Twitter. If the person you blocked joins as a listener, they will appear in the participant list with a Blocked label under their account name. If the person you blocked joins as a speaker, they will also appear in the participant list with a Blocked label under their account name and you will see an in-app notification stating, \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cAn account you blocked has joined as a speaker.\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d If you are entering a Space that already has a blocked account as a speaker, you will also see a warning before joining the Space stating, \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cYou have blocked 1 person who is speaking.\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d\nIf you are hosting or co-hosting a Space, people you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve blocked can\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t join and, if you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re added as a co-host during a Space, anyone in the Space who you blocked will be removed from the Space.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHow can I block someone in a Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWhile in a Space, select the account\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s profile photo to pull up the option menu. Select\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Block. This action will also block the account on Twitter. Blocking someone in a Space will not automatically remove them from the Space unless you are a host or co-host of the Space.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHow can I mute a speaker in a Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nTo mute a speaker in a live Space, select the account\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s profile photo, which will pull up an option menu. Select\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Mute their mic\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0and you will receive an in-app notification that will let you know the individual has been muted.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0You also have the option to mute all speakers in your Space at once.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHow can I see people in my Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHosts, speakers, and listeners can select the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n icon to see people in a Space.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Since Spaces are publicly accessible by anyone, it may also be possible for an unknown number of logged-out people to listen to a Space\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s audio without being listed as a guest in the Space.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHow can I report a Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nIf you think a Space violates the Twitter Rules, you can report it while in the Space by selecting the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0more\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n icon and selecting\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Report this Space. Anyone in the Space can report it. Speakers and listeners can report a Space and any account in a Space.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHow can I report a person in a Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nTo report an account in a Space, select the account\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s profile photo and then select\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Report. You will then need to choose the reason for reporting the account.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHow many people can speak in a Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nFor now, a maximum of 13 people (including the host and up to 2 co-hosts) can speak at the same time.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHow many people can listen in a Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nThere is no limit on the number of listeners.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat happens after a Space ends and is the data retained anywhere?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nSpaces are accessible while they are live; once ended, they will no longer be available publicly on Twitter. Twitter retains copies of audio from Spaces and\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0available captions for 30 days after a Space ends to review for violations of the Twitter Rules. If a Space is found to contain a violation, we extend the time we maintain a copy for\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0an additional 90 days (a total of 120 days after a Space ends) to allow people to appeal if they believe there was a mistake.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Twitter also uses Spaces content and data for analytics and research to improve the service.\nHosts may download copies of their Spaces for as long as we have them by using the Your Twitter Data download tool.\nLinks to Spaces that are shared out (e.g., via Tweet or DM) also contain some information about the Space, including the description, the identity of the hosts and others in the Space, as well as the Space\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s current state (e.g., scheduled, live, or ended). We make this and other information about Spaces available through the Twitter Developer Platform. For a detailed list of the information about Spaces we make available, check out our Spaces endpoints documentation.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWho can end a Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nThe host of a Space has the ability to end a Space. A Space may also end if it is found to be in violation of the Twitter Rules.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nDoes Spaces work for accounts with protected Tweets?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nAccounts with protected Tweets are not able to create Spaces. They are able to join and speak in other people\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s Spaces, and their presence will be visible to other participants.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nIs Spaces accessible for people who are deaf or hard of hearing?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nPeople in a Space can select the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Show captions\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0button to see automated live captions (with a few seconds of delay).\nCaptions only appear on-screen when a person is looking at a live Space. We do not show captions to a person if they have docked the Space to the bottom of their Twitter app or are off the app (although the audio will continue to play).\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHow is Twitter thinking about accessibility?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWe\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re collaborating internally with our accessibility teams and with an external accessibility vendor for review.\nSpaces will also release with accessibility for screen readers, though like any product, we\'ll continue to make additional improvements over time.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nDoes Spaces support captions or other accessibility options?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nPeople in a Space can navigate to the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0more\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n icon and select the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Show captions\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0button to see automated live captions (with a few seconds of delay).\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          Spaces Feedback Community\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWe\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re opening up the conversation and turning it over to the people who are participating in Spaces. This Community is a dedicated place for us to connect with you on all things Spaces, whether it\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s feedback around features, ideas for improvement, or any general thoughts.\nWho can join?\nAnyone on Spaces can join, whether you are a host, speaker, or listener.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nHow do I join the Community?\nYou can request to join the Twitter Spaces Feedback Community here. By requesting to join, you are agreeing to our Community rules.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nLearn more about Communities on Twitter.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          Community Spaces\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nAs a Community admin or moderator, you can create and host a Space for your Community members to join.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      Admins & moderators: How to create a Space\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nNavigate to the Community landing page.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nLong press on the Tweet Composer\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0and select the Spaces\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n icon.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nSelect Spaces and begin creating your Space by adding in a title, toggling on record Space (optional), and adding relevant topics.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nInvite admins, moderators, and other people to be a part of your Space.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n            Step 1\n          \n\nNavigate to the Community landing page.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 2\n          \n\nSelect the Tweet Composer\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n and select the Spaces\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n icon.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 3\n          \n\nSelect Spaces and begin creating your Space by adding in a title, toggling on record Space (optional), and adding relevant topics.\n\n\n\n\n            Step 4\n          \n\nInvite admins, moderators, and other people to be a part of your Space.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n      Members: How to find a Community Space\n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\nIf a Community Space is live, you will see the Spacebar populate at the top of your Home timeline. To enter the Space and begin listening, select the live Space in the Spacebar.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          Community Spaces FAQ\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat are Community Spaces?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nCommunity Spaces allows creators to create Spaces to keep their members engaged and help new people discover and join their Community.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWho can host a Community Space?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nOnly some admins and moderators will be able to host a Space, using the Twitter for iOS and Twitter for Android apps. Community members cannot host or start a Space within a Community, but they can ask to be a speaker in the Space.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHow will I be notified if a Community Space is going live?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWhen an admin or moderator starts a Space, community members and their followers will be notified via their notifications tab as well as the Spacebar.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nAs a Community member, what happens when a Space is live within the Community I am a part of?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nMembers will receive a notification in their notifications tab and also see the Spacebar populate with the live Space. Members will also be marked as a member of the Community while the Space is live.\nNote: As we are currently testing with a small group, some members may not see a notification in their notifications tab.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nCan I join a Space if I am not a member of the Community?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nYes. You will see the purple Spacebar populated at the top of your Home timeline if a person you follow is either hosting or in the live Space.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nWhat Spaces will feel like\n\nSpaces Sensory Guide\n\nA sensory guide is an accessibility tool that identifies sensory stimuli that people may encounter in an environment.\nJoining a Space\n\n\nSensory guide of how joining a space might feel.\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\nSound Level\nMotion Level\nImagery Level\nInformation Level\n\n\nReceives invite via DM to join a space or sees an active space in Fleet line or timeline\nQuiet\nLow\nHigh\nHigh\n\n\nJoins space as a listener and enters a conversation\nMedium\nCaptions off: Low; Captions on: Medium\nCaptions off: Medium; Captions on: High\nCaptions off: Medium, Captions on: High\n\n\nRequests speaker privileges\nMedium\nLow\nMedium\nMedium\n\n\nUnmutes self and contributes to the conversation\nLoud\nCaptions off: Low; Captions on: Medium\nCaption off: Medium; Captions on: High\nCaption off: Medium; Captions on: High\n\n\nSpace ends or leaves conversation\nQuiet\nLow\nLow\nLow\n\n\n\n\nHosting a Space\n\nSensory guide of how hosting a Space might feel.\n\xc2\xa0\nSound Level\nMotion Level\nImagery Level\nInformation Level\nOpens Twitter app on iOS\nQuiet\nLow\nHigh\nHigh\nTaps "Start Space"\nQuiet\nLow\nMedium\nCaptions off: Medium, Captions on: High\nNames and starts Space\nQuiet\nLow\nMedium\nMedium\nLaunches Space, begins speaking as listeners join\nMedium to Loud\nCaptions off: Low; Captions on: Medium\nCaption off: Medium; Captions on: High\nCaption off: Medium; Captions on: High\nEnds Space\nQuiet\nLow\nLow\nLow\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nSpaces Social Narrative\n\nA social narrative is a simple story that describes social situations and social behaviors for accessibility.\nTwitter Spaces allows me to join or host live audio-only conversations with anyone.\n\n\n\n\nJoining a Space\n\n\n\n\n1. When I join a Twitter Space, that means I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll be a listener. I can join any Space on Twitter, even those hosted by people I don\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t know or follow.\n\n\n\n\n2. I can join a Space by selecting a profile photo with a purple, pulsing outline at the top of my timeline, selecting a link from someone\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s Tweet, or a link in a Direct Message (DM).\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n3. Once I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99m in a Space, I can see the profile photos and names of some people in the Space, including myself.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n4. I can hear one or multiple people talking at the same time. If it\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s too loud or overwhelming, I can turn down my volume.\n\n\n\n\n5. As a listener, I am not able to speak. If I want to say something, I can send a request to the host. The host might not approve my request though.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n6. If the host accepts my request, I will become a speaker. It may take a few seconds to connect my microphone, so I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll have to wait.\n\n\n\n\n7.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Now I can unmute myself and speak. Everyone in the Space will be able to hear me.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n8.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0When someone says something I want to react to, I can choose an emoji to show everyone how I feel. I will be able to see when other people react as well.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n9.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0I can leave the Space at any time. After I leave, or when the host ends the Space, I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll go back to my timeline.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nHosting\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0a Space\n\n\n\n\n1.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0When I start a Space, that means I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll be the host. Anyone can join my Space, even people I don\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t know and people I don\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t follow.\n\n\n\n\n2.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Once I start my space, it may take a few seconds to be connected, so I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll have to wait.\n\n\n\n\n3.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Now I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99m in my Space and I can see my profile photo. If other logged-in, people have joined, I will be able to see their profile photos, too.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n4.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0I will start out muted, which is what the microphone with a slash through it means. I can mute and unmute myself, and anyone in my Space, at any time.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n5.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0I can invite people to join my Space by sending them a Direct Message (DM), sharing the link in a Tweet, and by copying the link and sharing it somewhere else like in an email.\n\n\n\n\n6.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Up to 10 other people can have speaking privileges in my Space at the same time, and I can choose who speaks and who doesn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t. People can also request to speak, and I can choose to approve their request or not.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n7. When people join my Space, I may hear one or multiple people speaking at the same time. If I think they\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re too loud, I can turn down my volume or mute them.\n\n\n\n\n8. I can revoke speaking privileges, and block, remove or report someone if they\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re being offensive or disruptive to me or others.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n9.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0When someone says something I want to react to, I can choose an emoji to show everyone how I feel. I will be able to see when other people react as well.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n10. When I end my space it will end for everyone.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          Share this article\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nTweet'

=== b'FAQs' ===

b'FAQs\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\nWho can use Revue?How do I set up my Revue account?Who can show a newsletter on their Twitter profile?Is there another way to show my newsletter on Twitter aside from my profile?Can I control the display of the Tweet link preview?How does Twitter decide which image to show for link previews of newsletter issues? How does Twitter decide what text description to use for link previews of newsletter issues?What if I don\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t want my subscriber count to be displayed?What does it look like for my followers when I Tweet my Revue profile or newsletter issue?What happens if other people on Twitter Tweet my Revue profile or newsletter issue?Is there a fee for sending a newsletter?Is payout based solely on subscribers or are there other factors?How much of a payout do creators on Revue receive?Can I change the price of my monthly subscription?Can newsletter creators see their subscribers\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 Twitter-affiliated email addresses?Will newsletter creators receive their subscribers\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 Twitter accounts?What kind of analytics are shared?How do readers unsubscribe from a newsletter?Can subscribers subscribe directly to other newsletter platforms from creators\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 Twitter profiles?Are there any rules regarding Revue newsletter content?\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nWho can use Revue?\n\nAnyone can sign up to have a Revue newsletter.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nNote: Signing up for and using Revue is subject to Revue\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s Terms of Service and Privacy Policy.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nHow do I set up my Revue account?\n\nGo to the Revue signup page and then follow the steps to set up your account. Learn more about managing your Revue account.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nWho can show a newsletter on their Twitter profile?\n\nAnyone on Twitter who has a Revue newsletter can show it on their profile. Once the creator\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s Twitter account is connected to Revue, they can navigate to their settings on Revue to control the display of this feature.\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nIs there another way to show my newsletter on Twitter aside from my profile?\n\nYes, you can share it through Tweets. When composing a Tweet, add the link to your Revue profile, and Twitter will automatically generate a link preview for you. If you want to show a specific issue of your newsletter instead, just add the link to the issue you want to show and Twitter will generate a link preview of the issue.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nCan I control the display of the Tweet link preview?\n\nThe link preview will display helpful information about your Revue newsletter including the newsletter or issue title, newsletter or issue description, your Revue profile image, and subscriber count.\nTo edit your newsletter title, description, or profile image, go to your Revue account. Once logged in, navigate to your profile picture in the top-right corner and go to Account settings > Profile. Then scroll down and select what you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99d like to edit.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nTo edit your issue title, you need to change the subject line of that issue. Go to your Revue account and log in. Next, navigate to the Issues page. To edit the title of a draft, tap Edit. To edit the title of a published issue, tap or click on the drop-down arrow to the right of the issue in question, and select Edit issue. In both cases, change the text next to where it says Subject to your new desired issue title, and the page will auto-save.\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nHow does Twitter decide which image to show for link previews of newsletter issues?\n\nIf you have a specific image you would like to use as your thumbnail, you can upload that image when scheduling or sending a newsletter. The preview will use that selected image.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0If you have not specified an image for the thumbnail, Twitter will show the first image used in the newsletter issue.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0If the issue being shared doesn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t have an image, Twitter will show your Revue profile image.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Please remember only to use images that you have the right to use, in accordance with Revue\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s Terms of Service.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nHow does Twitter decide what text description to use for link previews of newsletter issues?\n\nIf you set a preheader for that issue, Twitter will show the preheader in the link preview. Learn how to add a preheader to your issues.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nIf no preheader is set, Twitter will use the introductory text in the issue.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nIf no introductory text is set, Twitter will use the Issues Description from your Revue profile settings.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nWhat if I don\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t want my subscriber count to be displayed?\n\nTo hide your subscriber count, go to your Revue account and navigate to Account Settings > Settings > Subscriber Count. Select Hide the number of subscribers on my profile page.\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nWhat does it look like for my Twitter followers when I Tweet my Revue profile or newsletter issue?\n\nWhen you share a link to your Revue profile, followers who click the link will see a Subscribe call-to-action button in the Tweet that appears on their timeline.\nWhen you share a link to a newsletter issue, your followers will also see a Subscribe call-to-action button when they return to their timeline.\nFor people who already subscribe to your newsletter, they will instead see an option to read the latest issue.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nWhat happens if other people on Twitter Tweet my Revue profile or newsletter issue?\n\nPeople on Twitter will see the same link previews described above, in their timelines, and will have the option to subscribe or read an issue.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nIs there a fee for sending a newsletter?\n\nNo, you can send a newsletter for free.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nIs payout based solely on subscribers or are there other factors?\n\nCreators on Revue have full control over whether to charge for their content. They decide on the monthly price of their paid newsletters and can offer discounts.\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nHow much of a payout do creators on Revue receive?\n\nWe\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll only charge 5% of your revenue. You\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll also be subject to processing fees by our payment processor. Twitter does not have control over the transaction fee nor currency exchange rates imposed by the payment processor. Read more about how pricing works on Revue.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nCan I change the price of my monthly subscription?\n\nYou can make edits at any time through Account settings on Revue.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nCan newsletter creators see their subscribers\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 Twitter-affiliated email addresses?\n\nYes, in order for a reader to subscribe to a newsletter from a creator\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s Twitter profile they must consent to sharing their email address with the creator. If a Twitter-affiliated email changes later, it will not be updated in Revue. If a subscriber does not have a Twitter-affiliated email address they will be asked to share their email with Revue, and those email addresses will be shared with newsletter creators.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nWill newsletter creators receive their subscribers\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 Twitter accounts?\n\nNothing relating to subscribers\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 Twitter accounts is shared with newsletter creators beyond the subscribers\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 Twitter-affiliated email addresses. In order to subscribe to a newsletter, subscribers are informed that by subscribing, the email address associated with their Twitter account will be shared with the newsletter through the Revue service.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nNote: While Twitter accounts are not shared with creators, creators can potentially identify subscribers\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 Twitter accounts using subscribers\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 email addresses.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nWhat kind of analytics are shared?\n\nRevue offers email analytics and unique engagement insights. Learn more about newsletter performance and analytics.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nHow do readers unsubscribe from a newsletter?\n\nThey can tap or click on the Unsubscribe or Manage subscription link in any email received from the creator.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nCan subscribers subscribe directly to other newsletter platforms from creators\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 Twitter profiles?\n\nNo, this feature is currently exclusive to Revue newsletters.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nAre there any rules regarding Revue newsletter content?\n\nAll content published with Revue must follow the Revue Terms of Service and Privacy Policy, and the Twitter Rules and policies.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Revue is intended to support a wide range of editorial content, but it is not meant to be used for publications that primarily exist to host promotions, giveaways, or similar activities.'

=== b'Building a Twitter community with purpose' ===

b'My path into digital community building was carved out for me by my parents, in real life. My community,\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0#blkcreatives\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0(pronounced\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0hashtag Black creatives) reflects the values they modeled in their partnership: honesty, relatability, respect, and authenticity \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93 and Twitter has been the tool we use to build out those values, influencing a generation to use their work for the betterment of everyone around them, online and off.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\nWhen my mother married my stepfather by law, but my Dad by love, they decided to both leave their current homes and find a middle ground. We were coming from Chicago, my first hometown; their compromise made Memphis my second. It was closer to our Mississippi roots and far enough away from the city for me to appreciate taking alternate routes.'

=== b'Building a Twitter community with purpose' ===

b'Our consistent traveling from one home to another during my childhood meant that I was always being introduced to a new cast of characters in the story of my life. But after graduating from college, I didn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t see any stories that reflected the reality that I wanted to actually live. That\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s what inspired me to create\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0#blkcreatives. The heart of this brand is a virtual community of Black creative professionals looking to create full, healthy, and sustainable lives \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93 much like what my parents set out to do.'

=== b'Building a Twitter community with purpose' ===

b'Twitter has become a vital tool for how we not only build, but sustain the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0#blkcreatives\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0community. My parents\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 strategy, experiences, and perspectives, was a strong example for me at 10-years-old. Who I am is a direct reflection of their decision to build a life in the South, and it created my desire to observe the details in all of my surroundings, and ultimately fueled my love for storytelling.\nI\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99m someone who\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s always been a bit of an outlier in the digital industry, but Twitter has opened the door to opportunities for me, which in turn have allowed me to hold the door open for others. In the middle of the wildest summer ever \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93 summer 2020 \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93 something even wilder happened. Two of my\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Tweets were turned into billboards\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0to support Black Lives Matter. This was already a big deal, but what I didn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t expect is how much it raised the visibility of our mission. Now, I know that sounds like a clich\xc3\x83\xc2\xa9, but during a time of complete lockdown, seeing a physical, tangible statement meant everything to me.'

=== b'Building a Twitter community with purpose' ===

b'The response to it was enormous and really served as a proof of concept for me. And because our visibility was raised, it made it easier for people to support our mission of empowering and uplifting Black creatives from a financial, emotional, AND mental standpoint. From that moment we were able to not only donate funds to those in need but we also were able to connect creatives to viable opportunities by way of our\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0job board\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0and direct referrals.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0@blkcreatives\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0is so special to our industry because we take every opportunity and resource that\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s given to us, and pour it back into our community in some way. We create with an intention to serve this demographic of Black creatives \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93 a demo that is often commodified before they are genuinely supported. Our representation brings our humanity to the forefront. Beyond black squares and diversity and inclusion causes, there are real, actual people who need support and we\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re committed to sharing and telling their stories. Context is just as important as content, especially in this digital age.\nTwitter has also allowed us to act as an amplifier for the missions that elevate what really matters. Through creating intentional digital Twitter-only experiences like our infamous\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Twitter chats. They\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve literally been the reason why our community has gained so much visibility on Twitter. Once you find a way to nurture your community on Twitter, the possibilities will reveal themselves. Our Twitter chats have also been the key to staying constantly engaged with how our community is feeling and how we can support them.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWhen I think of the stories that reflect our mission, I think about\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Michell Clark. Since 2015, Michell has been a guest at least 3 times for our Twitter chats and our friendship began through this platform. As a writer who writes affirmations for Black creatives, through\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0our chats and connection on Twitter, we\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve been able to watch him continuously reach new heights while empowering us. Or I think about\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Lisa Beasley. Another life-long friend that I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve met through our Twitter chats. Last November, after witnessing her hilarious Margaret Thatcher impression, I urged her to share it on Twitter and we\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99d amplify it. The video went viral with millions of views and that moment has led to incredible opportunities for her. I also think about\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Ariana Walton Smith, a content creator who I referred to for a position at\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0We Are Rosie. Through Twitter, We Are Rosie\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Kiana Pirouz\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0connected with me and the referral not only resulted in a new career level for Ariana but also a valuable team experience for a company doing amazing, necessary work. I also think about\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Nefertiti, a Memphis hair care expert, that I was referred to via Twitter.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n@blkcreatives\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0contribution to this industry is best told through the community we serve and their stories. What diversity fails to recognize, is that behind the statistics and data around race, Black creators are real people, with real stories, struggles, experiences, and insight. It doesn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t take into account the fullness of our humanity and our range. @blkcreatives is dedicated to translating that value via our stories and the other communities we inspire to do the same. When you inspire @blkcreatives, we pour that into other Black creatives and their ecosystems which strengthen our culture holistically as well as financially and mentally.'

=== b'Amplifying Latinx representation, one Tweet at a time' ===

b'We\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re so excited to chat with you! Let\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s start with a little about you.\n\nI work in gaming, I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99m 30 years old, and I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve been in the space for about a decade. I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve been all over the gaming industry, and a passion for learning everything I can has seen my career hop from game development, to the software side, to streaming, and now to esports. I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve been gaming since I was a kid. In 1996, my dad bought me an N64 for Christmas and I was hooked. My Latinidad and gaming were always intermixed. When my cousins visited from Colombia, they would help me beat Zelda. I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99d show my tios my Pokemon collection. And even during our rehearsal for my Quincea\xc3\x83\xc2\xb1era, my friends and I would try to finish early so we could all play Smash Bros together.'

=== b'Amplifying Latinx representation, one Tweet at a time' ===

b'Was there a specific experience that highlighted the need for more Latinx representation in the gaming industry?\n\n\r\nI love marketing and events, but at times, it was difficult to deal with the microaggressions I faced as Latinx and being homesick for a country I couldn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t visit often. My heart hurt and I felt unheard. But it\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s never been in me to rest or sit still, so I decided to do something about it.\nEvery year, at every convention I went to, I would meet a Latinx person. The reactions would vary: hugging, dancing, or sharing stories of camaraderie, like \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cOnly Latinx person at your studio too, huh?\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d These moments were fleeting and would lead to a Twitter connection or maybe a coffee at the next convention, but never something more. I would count on my fingers the number of Latinx folks I knew, and sometimes I counted them when I was frustrated with a work situation or feeling isolated in my Latinidad. I knew there were other Latinx, but I didn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t know where I could find them. There weren\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t many resources for Latinx professionals back then, and I didn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t see places for them to interconnect outside of work.'

=== b'Amplifying Latinx representation, one Tweet at a time' ===

b'How did Latinx in Gaming get started?\n\r\nI started\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Latinx in Gaming, as a panel. I invited folks through Twitter to join me at GDC (Game Developers Conference). The panel was an incredible success! All these feelings I had on being lonely, being unseen, and being unheard weren\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t just shared \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93 they were a common experience in the Latinx community. We felt we had to keep that momentum going.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nLatinx in Gaming grew. We hosted panels at every convention, we met most of our contacts through conventions or Twitter and kept in touch there. We built out a Discord, a Facebook page, a LinkedIN. We kept speaking publicly, kept talking to our people, and kept asking other Latinx professionals to share their stories.\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWe\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re so glad you turned to Twitter to create\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0@latinosingaming! Were there any particular strategies you used to build up the community?\n\r\nHonestly, our strategy was a couple different pieces. Firstly, we consistently asked our audience to share with us other Latinx folks of note. \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cGive us women in the space you admire, tell us people who uplift you.\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d We would follow those folks or message them. Anytime we put on an event, we\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99d Tweet that we want volunteers, usually with a form. We\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve developed our network overtime this way. There\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s still a ton of folks we haven\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t reached, but Twitter helped us grow from 5 followers to 5,000. Finally, it was important to be unafraid to share voices. When we first started out, we tried to avoid \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cspamming\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d the timeline. But we realized that by Retweeting Latinx folks, and Retweeting responses to us, we were building an audience and giving folks a platform to see and find each other. We were a mouthpiece and it was okay to be loud.\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nDo you have a go-to Twitter feature(s) you love to use?\n\nWe love\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0scheduling Tweets. We do a lot of things throughout the months that show off Latinx voices and having it all scheduled out in advance helps us be organized and makes our Tweets look super polished.'

We Tweeted\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Lists\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0upon Lists of developers to follow, we uplifted folks who were looking to hire, we uplifted folks looking for a job. === b'How Black Girl Gamers used Twitter to change the game' ===

b"Twitter has played a major part in the growth of Black Girl Gamers \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93 we wouldn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t be where we are without it. It's the platform that houses all the discussions, updates and news in the Gaming industry, but also allows you to express your personality.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nGaming is...interesting. Since a young age, I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve enjoyed escaping to various fantasy worlds but it was always a matter of time until I was brought back to reality. When I was young, it was in the form of absence of Black women characters \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93 one or two would grace the screen but as stereotypes that were so predictable, bland, and offensive. Now don\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t get me wrong, I didn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t expect Black women to be in Crash Bandicoot (a game about a spinning marsupial), but our appearances were so far and few between that, at one point, I believed gaming to be a completely white male hobby.\xc3\x82"

=== b'How Black Girl Gamers used Twitter to change the game' ===

b'When online gaming arrived, it brought along with it another forum for white male gamers to flex their colonial attitudes towards anything they deem of value; once again taking me out of the fantasy world and into reality. And when gaming conversations were born online, they brought that toxicity with them. I grew tired and stopped gaming online for years, but after seeing some male \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cfriends\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d from university create their own gaming channels with truly mediocre content and borderline offensive commentary \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x93 I started my own channel along with my personal Twitter page.'

=== b'How Black Girl Gamers used Twitter to change the game' ===

b'Though I abandoned my gaming channel endeavours to focus on creating\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Black Girl Gamers, it was via my\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0personal Twitter page\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0that I met friends like\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0@ljay90, most likely via hashtags like\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0#blackgamers, who in turn introduced me to fellow Black women gamers such as\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0@junaebenne,\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0@chasinglux, and\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0@astylishjedi\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0(who still helps manage our Twitter page) who later became the first Community Management team for Black Girl Gamers. They, like myself, felt either annoyed, ostracised, invisible, undervalued or needed camaraderie.\nIf I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99m being honest, I was bored of some of the conversations about race and gaming that I saw online. They were so frequently rooted in assimilation or fear of rocking developers\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 boats. I felt concessions were made on the behalf of Black gamers to comfort developer fragility that would hold us back in the long run. Ultimately, something was missing from these discussions, and in hindsight it\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s only now that I realise it was the vim. To be vocal online meant braving a tidal wave of whitesplaining, mansplaining, or racist responses. I wanted\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Black Girl Gamers\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0to contribute positively to the narrative so I created the Twitter handle. Having a Twitter page brought visibility to our experiences and opinions to many, including those who disagreed with our Tweets. But, it isn\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t always serious stuff, I love to crack jokes and often make threads such as \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cIf Beyonc\xc3\x83\xc2\xa9 were a Fantasy RPG character\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d because there was an unspoken feeling that Black pop culture was juxtaposed to gaming culture at times.'
