=== b'Glorification of violence policy' ===

b'Overview\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nMarch 2019\nYou may not threaten violence against an individual or a group of people. We also prohibit the glorification of violence.\nGlorifying violent acts could inspire others to take part in similar acts of violence. Additionally, glorifying violent events where people were targeted on the basis of their protected characteristics (including: race, ethnicity, national origin, sexual orientation, gender, gender identity, religious affiliation, age, disability, or serious disease) could incite or lead to further violence motivated by hatred and intolerance. For these reasons, we have a policy against content that glorifies acts of violence in a way that may inspire others to replicate those violent acts and cause real offline harm, or events where members of a protected group were the primary targets or victims.\n\n\nWhat is in violation of this policy?\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nUnder this policy, you can\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99t glorify, celebrate, praise or condone violent crimes, violent events where people were targeted because of their membership in a protected group, or the perpetrators of such acts. We define glorification to include praising, celebrating, or condoning statements, such as \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cI\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99m glad this happened\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d, \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cThis person is my hero\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d, \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cI wish more people did things like this\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d, or \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cI hope this inspires others to act\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nViolations of this policy include, but are not limited to, glorifying, praising, condoning, or celebrating:\nviolent acts committed by civilians that resulted in death or serious physical injury, e.g., murders, mass shootings;attacks carried out by terrorist organizations or violent extremist groups (as defined by our terrorism and violent extremism policy); andviolent events that targeted protected groups, e.g., the Holocaust, Rwandan genocide.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWhat is not a violation of this policy?\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nOur focus is on preventing the glorification of violence that could inspire others to replicate violent acts, as well as violent events where protected groups were the primary targets or victims. Exceptions may be made for violent acts by state actors, where violence was not primarily targeting protected groups.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWho can report violations of this policy?\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nAnyone can report potential violations of this policy, whether they have a Twitter account or not.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nHow can I report violations of this policy?\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nIn-app\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nYou can report this content for review in-app as follows:\nSelect Report Tweet from the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n icon.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Select It\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s abusive or harmful.Select Threatening violence or physical harm.Select the relevant option depending on who you are reporting on behalf of.Select up to 5 Tweets to report for review.Submit your report.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nDesktop\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nYou can report this content for review via desktop as follows:\nSelect Report Tweet from the\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n icon.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Select It\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s abusive or harmful.Select Threatening violence or physical harm.Select the relevant option depending on who you are reporting on behalf of.Select up to 5 Tweets to report for review.Submit your report.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nReport form\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nYou can also report this content for review via our abusive behavior reporting form, by selecting the Harassment option.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWhat happens if you violate this policy?\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nThe consequences for violating our glorification of violence policy depends on the severity of the violation and the account\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s previous history of violations.\nThe first time you violate this policy, we will require you to remove this content. We will also temporarily lock you out of your account before you can Tweet again. If you continue to violate this policy after receiving a warning, your account will be permanently suspended. If you believe that your account was suspended in error, you can submit an appeal.\n\n\nAdditional resources\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nLearn more about our range of enforcement options and our approach to policy development and enforcement.\nTo learn about the link between glorifying violent acts and offline harm, you can refer to the research of Susan Benesch: Countering Dangerous Speech: New Ideas for Genocide Prevention and the Dangerous Speech Project.'


=== b'Copyright policy' ===

b'What types of copyright complaints does Twitter respond to?\n\nTwitter responds to copyright\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0complaints submitted under the Digital Millennium Copyright Act (\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cDMCA\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d). Section 512 of the DMCA outlines the statutory requirements necessary for formally reporting copyright infringement, as well as providing instructions on how an affected party can appeal a removal by submitting a compliant counter-notice.\nTwitter will respond to reports of alleged copyright infringement, such as allegations concerning the unauthorized use of a copyrighted image as a profile or header photo, allegations concerning the unauthorized use of a copyrighted video or image uploaded through our media hosting services, or Tweets containing links to allegedly infringing materials. Note that not all unauthorized uses of copyrighted materials are infringements (see our\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0fair use\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0article for more information).\nIf you are concerned about the use of your brand or entity\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s name, please review\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Twitter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s trademark policy. If you are concerned about a parody, newsfeed, commentary, or fan account, please see the relevant policy\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0here. These are generally not copyright issues.\n\n\n\n\n\nAm I a copyright holder? How do I know?\n\nIf you are unsure whether you hold rights to a particular work, please consult an attorney or another adviser as Twitter cannot provide legal advice. There are plenty of resources to learn more about copyright law including\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0http://copyright.gov,\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0https://lumendatabase.org/, and\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0http://www.eff.org/issues/bloggers/legal/liability/IP, to name a few.\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat to consider before submitting a copyright complaint\n\nBefore submitting a copyright complaint to us, please consider whether or not the use could be considered\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0fair use.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nIf you have considered fair use, and you still wish to continue with a copyright complaint, you may want to first reach out to the user in question to see if you can resolve the matter directly with the user. You can reply to the user\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s Tweet or send the user a Direct Message and ask for them to remove your copyrighted content without having to contact Twitter.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nPrior to submitting a formal complaint with Twitter, please be aware that under 17 U.S.C. \xc3\x82\xc2\xa7 512(f), you may be liable for any damages, including costs and attorneys\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 fees incurred by us or our users, if you knowingly materially misrepresent that material or activity is infringing. If you are unsure whether the material you are reporting is in fact infringing, you may wish to contact an attorney before filing a notification with us.\nNote: In general, the photographer and NOT the subject of a photograph is the actual rights holder of the resulting photograph. If you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re unsure whether or not you own the copyrights to a work, or if you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re infringing upon someone else\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s work, please consult an attorney or another advisor.\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat information do you need to process a copyright complaint?\n\nTo submit a notice of claimed copyright infringement, you will need to provide us with the following information:\nA physical or electronic signature (typing your full name will suffice) of the copyright owner or a person authorized to act on their behalf;Identification of the copyrighted work claimed to have been infringed (e.g., a link to your original work or clear description of the materials allegedly being infringed upon);Identification of the infringing material and information reasonably sufficient to permit Twitter to locate the material on our website or services;Your contact information, including your address, telephone number, and an email address;A statement that you have a good faith belief that the use of the material in the manner asserted is not authorized by the copyright owner, its agent, or the law; andA statement that the information in the complaint is accurate, and, under penalty of perjury, that you are authorized to act on behalf of the copyright owner.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nIf you are reporting the content of a Tweet, please give us a direct link to that Tweet. Or please specify if the alleged infringement is in the header, avatar, etc. A LINK TO A PROFILE PAGE IS INSUFFICIENT FOR TWITTER TO IDENTIFY INFRINGING MATERIALS.\n\n\n\n\n\nHow do I file a copyright complaint?\n\nYou can report alleged copyright infringement by visiting Twitter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s Help Center and\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0filing a copyright complaint.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0If you are logged in to twitter.com, you can visit the Twitter Help Center directly from your Twitter account by clicking the \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x98Help\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 link located in the sidebar.\nFiling a DMCA complaint is the start of a pre-defined legal process. Your complaint will be reviewed for accuracy, validity, and completeness. If your complaint has satisfied these requirements, we will take action on your request - which includes forwarding a full copy of your notice (including your name, address, phone and email address) to the user(s) who posted the allegedly infringing material in question.\nIf you are concerned about your contact information being forwarded, you may wish to use an agent to report for you.\nPlease be aware that under 17 U.S.C. \xc3\x82\xc2\xa7 512(f), you may be liable for any damages, including costs and attorneys\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 fees incurred by us or our users, if you knowingly materially misrepresent that material or activity is infringing. If you are unsure whether the material you are reporting is in fact infringing, you may wish to contact an attorney before filing a copyright complaint.\n\n\n\n\n\nHow are claims processed?\n\nWe process copyright complaints in the order in which they are received. Once you\'ve submitted your ticket, we will email you a ticket confirmation. If you do not receive a ticket confirmation that means we did not receive your complaint and you should re-submit your complaint. However, please note, submitting duplicate copyright complaints will result in a delay in processing.\nIf we decide to remove or disable access to the material, we will notify the affected user(s) and provide them with a full copy of the reporter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s complaint (including the provided contact information) along with instructions on how to file a counter-notice. We will also forward a redacted copy of the complaint to\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Lumen, with your personal information removed.\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat information gets forwarded to the reported user(s)? \n\nIf we remove or disable access to the materials reported in a copyright complaint, the reported user(s) will receive a copy of the complaint, including the reporter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s full name, email, street address, and any other information included in the complaint.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nIf you are uncomfortable sharing your contact information with the reported user(s), you may wish to consider appointing an agent to submit your DMCA notice on your behalf. Your agent will be required to submit the DMCA notice with valid contact information, and identify you as the content owner that they are representing.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat happens next?\n\nTwitter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s response to copyright complaints may include the removal or restriction of access to allegedly infringing material. If we remove or restrict access to user content in response to a copyright complaint, Twitter will make a good faith effort to contact the affected account holder with information concerning the removal or restriction of access, including a full copy of the complaint, along with instructions for filing a counter-notice.\nIf you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve not yet received a copy of the copyright complaint regarding the content removed from your account, please respond to the support ticket we sent you.\nIn an effort to be as transparent as possible regarding the removal or restriction of access to user-posted content, we clearly mark withheld Tweets and media to indicate to viewers when content has been withheld (examples below). We also send a redacted copy of each copyright complaint and counter-notice that we process to Lumen, where they are posted to a public-facing website (with your personal information removed).\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          My content was removed from Twitter\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\nWhy did I receive a copyright complaint?\n\nIf you receive a copyright complaint, it means that access to the content described in the complaint has been restricted. Please take the time to read through our correspondence to you, which includes information on the complaint we received as well as instructions on how to file a counter-notice. Please ensure that you are monitoring the email address associated with your Twitter account.\nTip: Removing the material reported in a copyright complaint will not resolve that complaint\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat if I want to contest the takedown?\n\nIf you believe that the materials reported in the copyright\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0complaints\r\nwere misidentified or removed in error, you may send us a counter-notification(s)\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0through our Help Center. A counter-notice is a request for Twitter to reinstate the removed material, and it has legal consequences. Alternatively, you may be able to seek a retraction of the copyright complaint from the reporter.\n\n\n\n\n\nHow do I seek a retraction?\n\nThe DMCA complaint you received includes the contact information of the reporter. You may want to reach out and ask them to retract their notice using our\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0retraction form. This is the fastest and most efficient means of resolving an unresolved copyright complaint. Alternatively, the reporter can also send a retraction notice to\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0copyright@twitter.com.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0 Such notice should include: (1) identification of the material that was disabled, and (2) a statement that the reporter would like to retract their DMCA notice.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0 A retraction is at the sole discretion of the original reporter, and only that reporter can issue a retraction.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0 If a portion of your tweet has been withheld, the violation will not be resolved just by deleting the remaining portion.\n\n\n\n\n\nWhen should I file a counter-notice?\n\nA counter-notice is a request for Twitter to reinstate the removed material, and is the start of a legal process that has legal consequences.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0 For example, submitting a counter notice indicates that you consent to the jurisdiction of a U.S. Federal court and that you consent to the disclosure of your personal information to the reporter and Lumen website.\nWith these considerations in mind, you may file a counter-notice if you believe that this material was misidentified, or you have a good faith belief that the material should not have been removed.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0 If you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re unsure whether or not you should file a counter-notice, you may want to consult with an attorney.\nTip:\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Re-posting material removed in response to a copyright complaint may result in permanent account suspension. If you believe the content was removed in error, please file a counter-notice rather than re-posting the material.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat information do you need to process a counter-notice?\n\nTo submit a counter-notice, you will need to provide us with the following information:\nA physical or electronic signature (typing your full name will suffice);Your full name, address (including country), telephone number, and for verification purposes, your Twitter username and associated email;Identification of the material that has been removed or to which access has been disabled, and the location at which the material appeared before that removal or disabling (the description from the copyright notice will suffice);A statement under penalty of perjury that you have a good faith belief that the material was removed or disabled as a result of mistake or misidentification of the material to be removed or disabled; andOne of the following jurisdictional consent statements:\n(If your address is in the United States)\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9cI consent to the jurisdiction of the Federal District Court for the judicial district in which my address is located and I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll accept service of process from the person who provided notice under 17 U.S.C. 512 (c)(1)(C) or an agent of such person.\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x9d\nOR\n(If your address is outside of the United States)\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n"I consent to any judicial district in which Twitter may be found, and I\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ll accept service of process from the person who provided notice under 17 U.S.C. 512 (c)(1)(C) or an agent of such person."\n\nTo submit a counter-notice, please provide all of the above information using our web form, located\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0here.\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat happens after I submit a counter-notice?\n\nUpon receipt of a valid counter-notice, we will promptly forward a copy to the person who filed the original notice. This means that the contact information that is submitted in your counter-notice will be shared to the person who filed the original notice.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nIf the copyright owner disagrees that the content was removed in error or misidentification, they may pursue legal action against you.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0 If we do not receive notice within 10 business days that the original reporter is seeking a court order to prevent further infringement of the material at issue, we may replace or cease disabling access to the material that was removed.\nWe cannot offer any legal advice. Should you have questions, please consult an attorney.\n\n\n\n\n\nFiling a copyright complaint or counter-notice is serious business!\n\nPlease think twice before submitting a claim or counter-notice, especially if you are unsure whether you are the actual rights holder or authorized to act on a rights holder\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s behalf. There are legal and financial consequences for fraudulent and/or bad faith submissions. Please be sure that you are the actual rights holder, or that you have a good faith belief that the material was removed in error, and that you understand the repercussions of submitting a false claim.\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat happens if my account receives one or more copyright complaints?\n\nIf multiple copyright complaints are received about an account, or other evidence suggests a pattern of repeat infringement, Twitter may suspend that account in accordance with our Repeat Infringer Policy.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Our Repeat Infringer Policy takes valid retractions and counter-notices into account. Users suspended under that policy may file a suspension appeal using\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0this form.\nAdditionally, re-posting material that was already removed in response to a copyright complaint, indicating where to access copyrighted material on third party websites, or certain other actions that demonstrate your account is intended solely or primarily to infringe the copyrighted material of others may result in permanent account suspension. If you are suspended on this basis, you may file an appeal using\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0this form. Please be aware that appealing a suspension does not guarantee your account will be reinstated.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n          Share this article\n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nTweet'


=== b'About Twitter limits' ===

b"Why have limits?\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nLimits alleviate some of the strain on the behind-the-scenes part of Twitter and reduce downtime and error pages. For the sake of reliability, we've placed some limits on the account actions below.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nCurrent Twitter limits\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nThe current technical limits for accounts are:\nDirect Messages (daily): The limit is 500 messages sent per day.Tweets: 2,400 per day. The daily update limit is further broken down into smaller limits for semi-hourly intervals. Retweets are counted as Tweets.Changes to account email: 4 per hour.Following (daily): The technical follow limit is 400 per day. Please note that this is a technical account limit only, and there are additional rules prohibiting aggressive following behavior.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Following (account-based): Once an account is following 5,000 other accounts, additional follow attempts are limited by account-specific ratios.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nThese limits include actions from all devices, including web, mobile, phone, API, etc. API requests from all third-party applications are tracked against the hourly API limit. People who use multiple third-party applications with their account will therefore reach the API limit more quickly.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nThese limits may be temporarily reduced during periods of heavy site usage. In such cases, we will post an update on the Twitter status site.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWhat happens if I hit a limit?\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nIf you do reach a limit, we'll let you know with an error message telling you which limit you've hit. For limits that are time-based (like the Direct Messages, Tweets, changes to account email, and API request limits), you'll be able to try again after the time limit has elapsed.\nThe Tweet limit of 2,400 updates per day is further broken down into semi-hourly intervals. If you hit your account update/Tweet limit, please try again in a few hours after the limit period has elapsed.\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nHaving trouble?\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nIf you've hit a follow limit, please see this follow limit troubleshooting article for more information."


=== b'How cookies are used on Twitter' ===

b"Cookies and similar technologies like pixels and local storage provide you with a better, faster, and safer experience on Twitter. Cookies are also used to operate our services, which include our websites, applications, APIs, pixels, embeds, and email communications. Specifically, Twitter uses these technologies to:\nKeep you logged in to Twitter.Deliver features and functionality of Twitter services.Save and honor your preferences.Personalize the content you see.Protect you against spam and abuse.Show you more relevant ads.Provide subscription features and distribute certain content.Understand how you interact with our services and where we can improve.Measure the effectiveness of our advertising and marketing.Rate how our services perform and identify bugs and other quality issues.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Gather data used to operate our business \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x94 from measuring our audience size to enforcing the Twitter Rules.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nWhat are cookies, pixels, and local storage?\nWhy do our services use these technologies?\nWhere are these technologies used?\nWhat are my privacy options?\nMore privacy options\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nWhat are cookies, pixels, and local storage?\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nCookies are small files placed on your computer as you browse the web or use a web-enabled app. We use cookies to operate our services, discover how people use our services, understand how to make them work better and more.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0See above for more examples of how we use cookies.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nPixels are small amounts of code placed on a web page, in a web-enabled app, or an email. We use pixels, some of which we provide to advertisers to place on their web properties, to learn whether you've interacted with specific web or email content \xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x94 as many services do. This helps us measure and improve our services and personalize your experience, including the ads and content you see.\nWe use local storage to save data on your computer or mobile device. We use data from local storage to turn on web navigation, maintain video player preferences, customize what we show you based on your past interactions with our services, remember your preferences, and measure ad effectiveness. We may also use local storage on other websites, where necessary to provide you certain features, to obtain information about your visits to those sites.\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nWhy do our services use these technologies?\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nCookies, pixels, and local storage work to operate and support our business, and to help provide you with an improved experience. They're used across the following categories:\nAuthentication and securityFunctionalityUser preferencesAnalyticsResearch and developmentPersonalized contentAdvertisingMarketingPersonalization across devices\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWithin each of these categories, cookies, pixels, and local storage help us:\nAuthentication and security\nAuthenticate your Twitter access to show you relevant content. They also help prevent unauthorized parties from accessing your account. We use these technologies to:\nLog you in to Twitter and our services.Help protect your security and the security of our services.Let you view content with limited distribution.Help us detect and fight spam, abuse, and other activities that break the Twitter Rules.\nFunctionality\nDeliver error messages, allow you to switch between accounts, coordinate our service across tabs in a browser, and provide certain features on partner websites.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nUser preferences\nRemember information about your browser and your preferences.\nAnalytics\nImprove and understand how people use our services, including buttons and widgets.Optimize your experience by understanding how you interact with our services, like when and how often you use them and what links you visit, and from where. (We may use Google Analytics to help us with this.)\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Count the number of people who have seen a particular Tweet, embedded Tweets, buttons, or timeline. Learn more.\nResearch and development\nGather data about how you use our services, including how our services perform. This helps us detect issues, understand where we may improve, or develop new products or services.Test updates to Twitter services, as well as build new features, functionality,\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0and services.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nPersonalized content\r\nPersonalize our services in areas like trends, stories, ads, and suggestions for people to follow with more relevant content. We also use:\nLocal storage to tell us which parts of your Twitter timeline you've viewed already so that we can show you new content.Cookies\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0to suggest who you might enjoy following based on your visits to websites with integrated Twitter services.\nAdvertising\r\nPersonalize ads and measure performance, like showing you ads and evaluating their effectiveness based on your visits to our ad partners' websites. This helps advertisers provide you with high-quality ads and content that may be more interesting to you. We'll also:\nDeliver ads, measure their performance, and make them more relevant to you based on criteria, like your activity on Twitter and visits to our ad partners' websites.Work with third-party advertising partners, including Google, to market our services.\nMarketing\nDeliver our email and web marketing campaigns and to understand our marketing\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0effectiveness.\nPersonalization across devices\nUnderstand which devices you used so that we can personalize your experience on all of your devices.\nKeep in mind, if you ever log in to Twitter with your device, we associate and will continue to associate that device with your account. This means whether or not you're logged in, we'll receive information about your\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0device(s) when information is shared by a partner, you visit twitter.com or third-party websites that integrate Twitter services, or you visit a Twitter advertiser's website or mobile application. Most commonly, IP addresses and the time we receive the data, are used to link that specific device with you.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nTo see more about the devices and web browsers associated with your Twitter account, take a look at Your Twitter Data when you're logged in and when you're logged out of your account.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nWhere are these technologies used?\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWe\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0(along with third parties) use these technologies on Twitter services, which includes our websites, applications, and services and on other websites, applications, and services that have integrated Twitter services, including third-party properties that incorporate our advertising technology. This includes our ad partners\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99 websites and sites that use our embeds, including embedded timelines. Third parties may also use these technologies, for example, when you click on links from Twitter services, view or interact with third-party content in Twitter services, or visit third-party websites that incorporate our advertising technology.\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nWhat are my privacy options?\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nWe're committed to giving you meaningful privacy options to control or limit how we, our partners, and other third-parties use cookies and cookie-related data:\nTwitter stores information about other websites where you've seen Twitter content or accessed our services. For most Twitter features you can adjust this by going to: Settings and privacy > Privacy and safety > Off-Twitter activity > Allow use of where you see Twitter content across the web.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0However, for certain paid subscription features, even if you make this adjustment we will still store certain information where doing so is necessary for that feature to work. We will tell you about this storage when you sign up for these features.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nIf you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99ve turned this off, or are in the EU, \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway or Switzerland, we won't store or use these web page visits to improve your experience in the future. However, if we've previously stored your web browsing history, we may continue to personalize your experience based on information we've already learned from that history.\nYou will always see ads on Twitter based on your Twitter activity. There are a variety of ways you can adjust the way Twitter uses your data for ads. You can use the following tools:\nPersonalized ads setting in Twitter\nAdjust your setting for use of off-Twitter data by going to Settings and privacy > Privacy and safety > Ads preferences > Personalized ads.Interest-based advertising for web\nOpt-out in your current browser through the Digital Advertising Alliance's consumer choice tool at optout.aboutads.info.Limit ad tracking for iOS version 13 and earlier\r\nTurn on this setting through your iOS device settings (precise instructions vary by version).\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Ads personalization for Android\r\nOpt out through your device settings (precise instructions vary by version).\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Allow apps to request to track for iOS version 14 and later\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\r\nTurn off the setting through your device settings (precise instructions vary by version).\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Personalize based on your inferred identity setting in Twitter\r\nAdjust the setting by going to Settings and privacy > Privacy and safety > Off-Twitter activity > Personalize based on your inferred identity. This controls whether we link your account to browsers or devices other than the ones you use to log into Twitter (or if you're logged out, whether we link the browser or device you're currently using to any other browsers or devices).Cookie settings through web browsers\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\r\nMost browsers will request your permission to use cookies. Note that if you turn off cookies entirely, Twitter services may not work correctly\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0or you might have trouble logging into twitter.com.\n\n\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\nMore privacy options\r\n \xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nAlong with optout.aboutads.info, you can read more about opting out of interest-based ads at networkadvertising.org/choices. Lastly, you can opt-out of interest-based Google ads using Google's Ads Settings.\n\n\n\n\nImportant: To view or change web settings for your Twitter account, you'll need to log in to the web browser. Changing your Twitter settings in the web browser when you\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99re logged out will only affect behavior on that browser while you aren't logged in to Twitter. Read our article on how to access your personalization and data settings for more."

=== b'Subscriptions policy' ===

b'Thank you for taking the time to learn about Twitter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s policy for\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Subscriptions on Twitter. Through Subscriptions, you can provide an extra level of content, access and conversation for paying subscribers.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nIn order to ensure that people and organizations can participate in the public conversation freely and safely, we have a set of policies all creators who utilize\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Subscriptions must adhere to, including eligibility requirements and content and conduct requirements.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nNote: We anticipate learning from our beta launch of Subscriptions, and we will update this policy based on learnings.\n\n\nBeta eligibility requirements\nBeta eligibility requirements for\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Subscriptions creators are defined below. These requirements have been developed to ensure that beta participants can derive the utmost value from the feature, reduce likelihood of conduct and content related harms for people on Twitter, and enable learning and iteration on the feature and policy in the future. Note that meeting these requirements does not guarantee acceptance as a Subscriptions creator.\nYou are 18 years of age or older.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nYou have a complete profile with an account name, a bio, a profile picture, and a header image.You have a verified email address. Learn how to verify your email address.You have secured your account by enabling\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0 two-factor authentication. Learn how to enable two-factor authentication.You do not have a history of repeatedly violating the Twitter user agreement or Twitter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s Content monetization standards.You have not previously been removed as an advertiser on Twitter for violations of our Ads policies or as a publisher on Twitter for violations of our brand safety policies.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Your profile does not feature the identity of another person, brand, or organization, nor does it use a fake identity that is intended to deceive others.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0 Profiles that feature animals or fictional characters are ineligible, unless directly affiliated with your brand or organization. Parody and fan accounts are not eligible for Subscriptions.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Your account is not a state-affiliated media account.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0You have a Twitter account that has been active for 3 months or more.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0You maintain 10,000 active followers or more.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0You have posted 25 Tweets in the past 30 days.\nSubscriptions\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0is currently only open to U.S. creators. Twitter prohibits individuals and entities from using\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Subscriptions in violation of applicable laws, regulations, and/or the Subscriptions creator terms.\n\n\nConduct and content requirements\n\nYour conduct and content must be in compliance with the Twitter user agreement, including Twitter Rules. Among other requirements drawn out of Twitter Rules:\nYou must not request money or engagements in exchange for content or behavior that is (a) illegal, or (b) physically, psychologically, informationally, or economically harmful to you, other people or animals. In other words, soliciting money or engagements in exchange for illegal or harmful content or behavior is prohibited.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0You must not engage in fraud or deception. Do not mislead people into engaging with or compensating you. This includes not misleading people about which people or what entities are receiving compensation associated with your profile.You must only monetize content that is original and authentic, or otherwise content that you have the rights to monetize. If you share third party content (as background audio, for example, in a video you post to your Subscriptions), you must have the appropriate legal rights to do so.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nYou must adhere to Twitter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s Content monetization standards for all\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Subscriptions content.You must comply with the Subscriptions creator terms.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0If you advertise on Twitter, you must follow Twitter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s Ads policies. (Note that you must not promote\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Subscriptions content through Twitter Ads.)If you are a part of Twitter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s Amplify Publisher Program, you must follow Twitter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s brand safety policies. (Note that\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Subscriptions content must not be monetized through the Twitter Amplify Program.)\n\r\nEnforcement philosophy\n\nAll\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Subscriptions creators must comply with the requirements described and referenced on this page. Should you violate any one of these requirements, act in a manner directly counter to Twitter\xc3\xa2\xc2\x80\xc2\x99s purpose or principles, or otherwise act in a way we deem potentially harmful to Twitter or its customers, we may take some or all of the enforcement actions outlined below.\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nEligibility requirement enforcement\nIf you do not meet eligibility requirements, you will not be able to be a Subscriptions creator. If you are initially accepted to be a\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Subscriptions creator but later Twitter finds that you do not meet eligibility requirements, we may pause your ability to participate.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\n\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nConduct and content requirement enforcement\nDepending on context, severity, and history of violative behavior, we may:\nLimit amplification of your account via algorithmic recommendations to accounts that do not follow you.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nPause or permanently revoke your ability to participate as a\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Subscriptions creator.Pause or permanently revoke your access to other Twitter products that enable people to support you with their money.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Pause or permanently revoke your access to Twitter.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Hide violating content while it is awaiting removal.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0Remove, or require you to remove, violative content.\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\r\n\xc3\x82\xc2\xa0\nIf your account is compromised\nIf we detect that your account may be compromised, we will disable monetization features temporarily until your account is restored.'
